title="Eastern European Time">EET</a>)</td></tr><tr class="mergedbottomrow"><th class="infobox-label" scope="row"><div class="ib-country-fake-li">• Summer (<a href="/wiki/Daylight_saving_time" title="Daylight saving time">DST</a>)</div></th><td class="infobox-data"><span class="nowrap"><a href="/wiki/Coordinated_Universal_Time" title="Coordinated Universal Time">UTC</a>+3</span> (<a href="/wiki/Eastern_European_Summer_Time" title="Eastern European Summer Time">EEST</a>)</td></tr><tr><th class="infobox-label" scope="row">Date format</th><td class="infobox-data">dd.mm.yyyy</td></tr><tr><th class="infobox-label" scope="row"><a href="/wiki/Left-_and_right-hand_traffic" title="Left- and right-hand traffic">Driving side</a></th><td class="infobox-data">right</td></tr><tr><th class="infobox-label" scope="row"><a href="/wiki/Telephone_numbers_in_Ukraine" title="Telephone numbers in Ukraine">Calling code</a></th><td class="infobox-data"><a href="/wiki/Telephone_numbers_in_Ukraine" title="Telephone numbers in Ukraine">+380</a></td></tr><tr><th class="infobox-label" scope="row"><a href="/wiki/ISO_3166" title="ISO 3166">ISO 3166 code</a></th><td class="infobox-data"><a href="/wiki/ISO_3166-2:UA" title="ISO 3166-2:UA">UA</a></td></tr><tr><th class="infobox-label" scope="row"><a href="/wiki/Country_code_top-level_domain" title="Country code top-level domain">Internet TLD</a></th><td class="infobox-data"><div class="plainlist"><ul><li><a href="/wiki/.ua" title=".ua">.ua</a></li><li><a href="/wiki/.%D1%83%D0%BA%D1%80" title=".укр">.укр</a></li></ul></div></td></tr><tr><td class="infobox-full-data" colspan="2"><div class="ib-country-website"><b>Website</b><br/><a class="external text" href="https://ukraine.ua/" rel="nofollow">ukraine.ua</a></div></td></tr></tbody></table>
<p><b>Ukraine</b> (<a href="/wiki/Ukrainian_language" title="Ukrainian language">Ukrainian</a>: <span lang="uk">Україна</span>, <small><a href="/wiki/Romanization_of_Ukrainian" title="Romanization of Ukrainian">romanized</a>: </small><span title="Ukrainian-language romanization"><i lang="uk-Latn">Ukraïna</i></span>, <small>pronounced </small><span class="IPA" lang="uk-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/Ukrainian" title="Help:IPA/Ukrainian">[ʊkrɐˈjinɐ]</a></span> <span class="nowrap" style="font-size:85%">(<span class="unicode haudio"><span class="fn"><span style="white-space:nowrap;margin-right:.25em;"><a href="/wiki/File:Uk-%D0%A3%D0%BA%D1%80%D0%B0%D1%97%D0%BD%D0%B0_(2).oga" title="About this sound"><img alt="" data-file-height="20" data-file-width="20" decoding="async" height="11" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/11px-Loudspeaker.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/17px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/22px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 2x" width="11"/></a></span><a class="internal" href="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/b/be/Uk-%D0%A3%D0%BA%D1%80%D0%B0%D1%97%D0%BD%D0%B0_%282%29.oga" title="Uk-Україна (2).oga">listen</a></span></span>)</span>) is a country in <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Europe" title="Eastern Europe">Eastern Europe</a>. It is the <a href="/wiki/List_of_European_countries_by_area" title="List of European countries by area">second-largest European country</a> after <a href="/wiki/Russia" title="Russia">Russia</a>, which it borders <a href="/wiki/Russia%E2%80%93Ukraine_border" title="Russia–Ukraine border">to the east and northeast</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11"><a href="#cite_note-11">[a]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12"><a href="#cite_note-12">[11]</a></sup> Ukraine covers approximately 600,000 square kilometres (230,000 sq mi).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13"><a href="#cite_note-13">[b]</a></sup> Prior to the ongoing <a href="/wiki/Russo-Ukrainian_War" title="Russo-Ukrainian War">Russo-Ukrainian War</a>, it was the <a href="/wiki/List_of_European_countries_by_population" title="List of European countries by population">eighth-most populous country</a> in Europe, with a population of around 41 million people.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-14"><a href="#cite_note-14">[c]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-auto_6-1"><a href="#cite_note-auto-6">[6]</a></sup> It is also bordered by <a href="/wiki/Belarus" title="Belarus">Belarus</a> to the north; by <a href="/wiki/Poland" title="Poland">Poland</a>, <a href="/wiki/Slovakia" title="Slovakia">Slovakia</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Hungary" title="Hungary">Hungary</a> to the west; and by <a href="/wiki/Romania" title="Romania">Romania</a> and <a href="/wiki/Moldova" title="Moldova">Moldova</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-15"><a href="#cite_note-15">[d]</a></sup> to the southwest; with a coastline along the <a href="/wiki/Black_Sea" title="Black Sea">Black Sea</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Sea_of_Azov" title="Sea of Azov">Sea of Azov</a> to the south and southeast.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-18"><a href="#cite_note-18">[e]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Kyiv" title="Kyiv">Kyiv</a> is the nation's capital and <a href="/wiki/List_of_cities_in_Ukraine" title="List of cities in Ukraine">largest city</a>. The country's national language is <a href="/wiki/Ukrainian_language" title="Ukrainian language">Ukrainian</a>, and most people are also <a href="/wiki/Russian_language_in_Ukraine" title="Russian language in Ukraine">fluent in Russian</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19"><a href="#cite_note-19">[14]</a></sup>
</p><p>During the <a href="/wiki/Middle_Ages" title="Middle Ages">Middle Ages</a>, the area was a key centre of <a href="/wiki/East_Slavs" title="East Slavs">East Slavic culture</a> under the state of <a href="/wiki/Kievan_Rus%27" title="Kievan Rus'">Kievan Rus'</a>, which emerged in the 9th century and was ultimately destroyed by the <a href="/wiki/Mongol_invasion_of_Kievan_Rus%27" title="Mongol invasion of Kievan Rus'">Mongol invasions of the 13th century</a>. After the <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Galicia%E2%80%93Volhynia" title="Kingdom of Galicia–Volhynia">Kingdom of Galicia–Volhynia</a> emerged, the area was contested, divided, and ruled by a variety of external powers for the next 600 years, including the <a href="/wiki/Polish%E2%80%93Lithuanian_Commonwealth" title="Polish–Lithuanian Commonwealth">Polish–Lithuanian Commonwealth</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Austrian_Empire" title="Austrian Empire">Austrian Empire</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Ottoman_Empire" title="Ottoman Empire">Ottoman Empire</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Tsardom_of_Russia" title="Tsardom of Russia">Tsardom of Russia</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Cossack_Hetmanate" title="Cossack Hetmanate">Cossack Hetmanate</a> emerged in <a href="/wiki/Central_Ukraine" title="Central Ukraine">central Ukraine</a> in the 17th century, but was partitioned between Russia and Poland, and ultimately absorbed by the <a href="/wiki/Russian_Empire" title="Russian Empire">Russian Empire</a>. After the <a href="/wiki/Russian_Revolution" title="Russian Revolution">Russian Revolution</a>, a Ukrainian national movement re-emerged, and formed the <a href="/wiki/Ukrainian_People%27s_Republic" title="Ukrainian People's Republic">Ukrainian People's Republic</a> in 1917. This short-lived state was <a href="/wiki/Ukrainian%E2%80%93Soviet_War" title="Ukrainian–Soviet War">forcibly reconstituted</a> by the <a href="/wiki/Bolsheviks" title="Bolsheviks">Bolsheviks</a> into the <a href="/wiki/Ukrainian_Soviet_Socialist_Republic" title="Ukrainian Soviet Socialist Republic">Ukrainian Soviet Socialist Republic</a>, which became a founding member of the <a href="/wiki/Soviet_Union" title="Soviet Union">Soviet Union</a> in 1922. In the 1930s, millions of Ukrainians were killed by the <a href="/wiki/Holodomor" title="Holodomor">Holodomor</a>, a <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_Soviet_Union_(1927%E2%80%931953)" title="History of the Soviet Union (1927–1953)">Stalin-era</a> <a href="/wiki/Causes_of_the_Holodomor" title="Causes of the Holodomor">man-made famine</a>.
</p><p>Following the <a href="/wiki/Dissolution_of_the_Soviet_Union" title="Dissolution of the Soviet Union">collapse of the Soviet Union</a> in 1991, Ukraine regained independence and declared itself <a href="/wiki/Neutral_country" title="Neutral country">neutral</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-gska2.rada.gov.ua_20-0"><a href="#cite_note-gska2.rada.gov.ua-20">[15]</a></sup> forming a limited military partnership with the post-Soviet <a href="/wiki/Commonwealth_of_Independent_States" title="Commonwealth of Independent States">Commonwealth of Independent States</a>, while also joining the <a href="/wiki/Partnership_for_Peace" title="Partnership for Peace">Partnership for Peace</a> with <a href="/wiki/NATO" title="NATO">NATO</a> in 1994. In 2013, a series of mass demonstrations, known as the <a href="/wiki/Euromaidan" title="Euromaidan">Euromaidan</a>, erupted across Ukraine, eventually escalating into the <a href="/wiki/Revolution_of_Dignity" title="Revolution of Dignity">Revolution of Dignity</a> in 2014, which led to the establishment of a new government and <a href="/wiki/2014_pro-Russian_unrest_in_Ukraine" title="2014 pro-Russian unrest in Ukraine">pro-Russian unrest</a>. During this period, <a href="/wiki/Little_green_men_(Russo-Ukrainian_War)" title="Little green men (Russo-Ukrainian War)">unmarked Russian troops</a> invaded the <a href="/wiki/Crimea" title="Crimea">Crimean Peninsula</a>, which was later <a href="/wiki/Annexation_of_Crimea_by_the_Russian_Federation" title="Annexation of Crimea by the Russian Federation">annexed by Russia</a>; and pro-Russia unrest in Ukraine's <a href="/wiki/Donbas" title="Donbas">Donbas</a> culminated in Russia-backed separatists seizing territory throughout the region, sparking the <a href="/wiki/War_in_Donbas_(2014%E2%80%932022)" title="War in Donbas (2014–2022)">War in Donbas</a>. This series of events marked the beginning of the ongoing <a href="/wiki/Russo-Ukrainian_War" title="Russo-Ukrainian War">Russo-Ukrainian War</a>, and in a major escalation of the conflict in February 2022, Russia launched <a href="/wiki/2022_Russian_invasion_of_Ukraine" title="2022 Russian invasion of Ukraine">a full-scale invasion of Ukraine</a>. Since the outbreak of war with Russia in 2014, Ukraine has continued to seek closer economic, political, and military ties with the <a href="/wiki/Western_world" title="Western world">Western world</a>, including with the <a href="/wiki/Ukraine%E2%80%93United_States_relations" title="Ukraine–United States relations">United States</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ukraine%E2%80%93European_Union_relations" title="Ukraine–European Union relations">European Union</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Ukraine%E2%80%93NATO_relations" title="Ukraine–NATO relations">NATO</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-European_Commission_Trade_Ukraine_21-0"><a href="#cite_note-European_Commission_Trade_Ukraine-21">[16]</a></sup>
</p><p>Ukraine is a <a href="/wiki/Unitary_state" title="Unitary state">unitary republic</a> under a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Semi-presidential_system" title="Semi-presidential system">semi-presidential system</a> and a <a href="/wiki/Developing_country" title="Developing country">developing country</a>, ranking 77th on the <a href="/wiki/Human_Development_Index" title="Human Development Index">Human Development Index</a>. Ukraine is the <a href="/wiki/List_of_sovereign_states_in_Europe_by_GDP_(nominal)_per_capita" title="List of sovereign states in Europe by GDP (nominal) per capita">poorest country in Europe</a> by nominal GDP per capita,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-22"><a href="#cite_note-22">[17]</a></sup> and has high levels of <a href="/wiki/Corruption_in_Ukraine" title="Corruption in Ukraine">corruption</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-23"><a href="#cite_note-23">[18]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-24"><a href="#cite_note-24">[19]</a></sup> However, due to <a href="/wiki/Geography_of_Ukraine" title="Geography of Ukraine">its extensive fertile land</a>, pre-war Ukraine was <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_Ukraine" title="Economy of Ukraine">one of the largest grain exporters in the world</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-grain1_25-0"><a href="#cite_note-grain1-25">[20]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-grain2_26-0"><a href="#cite_note-grain2-26">[21]</a></sup> It is a founding member of the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">United Nations</a>, as well as a member of the <a href="/wiki/Council_of_Europe" title="Council of Europe">Council of Europe</a>, the <a href="/wiki/World_Trade_Organization" title="World Trade Organization">World Trade Organization</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Organization_for_Security_and_Co-operation_in_Europe" title="Organization for Security and Co-operation in Europe">OSCE</a>, and is in the <a href="/wiki/Accession_of_Ukraine_to_the_European_Union" title="Accession of Ukraine to the European Union">process</a> of joining the <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ukraine%E2%80%93NATO_relations" title="Ukraine–NATO relations">becoming</a> a <a href="/wiki/NATO" title="NATO">NATO</a> member.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-27"><a href="#cite_note-27">[22]</a></sup>
</p>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r886046785">.mw-parser-output .toclimit-2 .toclevel-1 ul,.mw-parser-output .toclimit-3 .toclevel-2 ul,.mw-parser-output .toclimit-4 .toclevel-3 ul,.mw-parser-output .toclimit-5 .toclevel-4 ul,.mw-parser-output .toclimit-6 .toclevel-5 ul,.mw-parser-output .toclimit-7 .toclevel-6 ul{display:none}</style><div class="toclimit-3"><div aria-labelledby="mw-toc-heading" class="toc" id="toc" role="navigation"><input class="toctogglecheckbox" id="toctogglecheckbox" role="button" style="display:none" type="checkbox"/><div class="toctitle" dir="ltr" lang="en"><h2 id="mw-toc-heading">Contents</h2><span class="toctogglespan"><label class="toctogglelabel" for="toctogglecheckbox"></label></span></div>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Etymology_and_orthography">Etymology and orthography</span></h2>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Name_of_Ukraine" title="Name of Ukraine">Name of Ukraine</a></div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Name_of_Ukraine" title="Name of Ukraine">name of <i>Ukraine</i></a> probably comes from the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Old_Slavic" title="Old Slavic">old Slavic</a> term for "borderland",<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28"><a href="#cite_note-28">[23]</a></sup> as does the word <i><a href="/wiki/Krajina" title="Krajina">krajina</a></i>.
</p><p><span class="anchor" id="the_Ukraine"></span>In the <a href="/wiki/English-speaking_world" title="English-speaking world">English-speaking world</a> during most of the 20th century, Ukraine (whether independent or not) was referred to as "the Ukraine".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-merriam-webster_29-0"><a href="#cite_note-merriam-webster-29">[24]</a></sup> This is because the word <i>ukraina</i> means "borderland"<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-30"><a href="#cite_note-30">[25]</a></sup> so the <a href="/wiki/Article_(grammar)" title="Article (grammar)">definite article</a> would be natural in the English language; this is similar to "<i><span title="Dutch-language text"><i lang="nl">Nederlanden</i></span></i>", which means "low lands" and is rendered in English as "<i>the</i> <a href="/wiki/Netherlands" title="Netherlands">Netherlands</a>".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-31"><a href="#cite_note-31">[26]</a></sup> However, since Ukraine's <a href="/wiki/Declaration_of_Independence_of_Ukraine" title="Declaration of Independence of Ukraine">declaration of independence</a> in 1991, this usage has become politicised and is now rarer, and <a href="/wiki/Style_guide" title="Style guide">style guides</a> advise against its use.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-UKrW812991TU_32-0"><a href="#cite_note-UKrW812991TU-32">[27]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33"><a href="#cite_note-33">[28]</a></sup> US ambassador <a href="/wiki/William_B._Taylor_Jr." title="William B. Taylor Jr.">William Taylor</a> said that using "the Ukraine" implies disregard for Ukrainian sovereignty.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34"><a href="#cite_note-34">[29]</a></sup> The official Ukrainian position is that "the Ukraine" is incorrect, both grammatically and politically.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BBC_News_Magazine_35-0"><a href="#cite_note-BBC_News_Magazine-35">[30]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span></h2>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/History_of_Ukraine" title="History of Ukraine">History of Ukraine</a></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_history">Early history</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Indo-European_migrations.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1372" data-file-width="3326" decoding="async" height="124" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b1/Indo-European_migrations.jpg/300px-Indo-European_migrations.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b1/Indo-European_migrations.jpg/450px-Indo-European_migrations.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b1/Indo-European_migrations.jpg/600px-Indo-European_migrations.jpg 2x" width="300"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Indo-European_migrations.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Early <a href="/wiki/Indo-European_migrations" title="Indo-European migrations">Indo-European migrations</a> from the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pontic_steppes" title="Pontic steppes">Pontic steppes</a> of present-day Ukraine and Russia<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-36"><a href="#cite_note-36">[31]</a></sup></div></div></div>
<p>Settlement by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Modern_humans" title="Modern humans">modern humans</a> in Ukraine and its vicinity dates back to 32,000 BC, with evidence of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gravettian_culture" title="Gravettian culture">Gravettian culture</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Crimean_Mountains" title="Crimean Mountains">Crimean Mountains</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-orig_37-0"><a href="#cite_note-orig-37">[32]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bbc_38-0"><a href="#cite_note-bbc-38">[33]</a></sup> By 4,500 BC, the <a href="/wiki/Neolithic" title="Neolithic">Neolithic</a> <a href="/wiki/Cucuteni%E2%80%93Trypillia_culture" title="Cucuteni–Trypillia culture">Cucuteni–Trypillia culture</a> was flourishing in wide areas of modern Ukraine, including <a href="/wiki/Trypillia" title="Trypillia">Trypillia</a> and the entire <a href="/wiki/Dnieper" title="Dnieper">Dnieper</a>-<a href="/wiki/Dniester" title="Dniester">Dniester</a> region. Ukraine is also considered to be the likely location of the first <a href="/wiki/Domestication_of_the_horse" title="Domestication of the horse">domestication of the horse</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39"><a href="#cite_note-39">[34]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-40"><a href="#cite_note-40">[35]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-41"><a href="#cite_note-41">[36]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cbc.ca_42-0"><a href="#cite_note-cbc.ca-42">[37]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Kurgan_hypothesis" title="Kurgan hypothesis">Kurgan hypothesis</a> places the Volga-Dnieper region of Ukraine and southern Russia as the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Urheimat" title="Urheimat">urheimat</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Proto-Indo-Europeans" title="Proto-Indo-Europeans">Proto-Indo-Europeans</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-43"><a href="#cite_note-43">[38]</a></sup> Early <a href="/wiki/Indo-European_migrations" title="Indo-European migrations">Indo-European migrations</a> from the Pontic steppes in the 3rd millennium BC spread <a href="/wiki/Yamnaya_culture" title="Yamnaya culture">Yamnaya</a> <a href="/wiki/Western_Steppe_Herders" title="Western Steppe Herders">Steppe pastoralist</a> ancestry and <a href="/wiki/Indo-European_languages" title="Indo-European languages">Indo-European languages</a> across large parts of Europe.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-44"><a href="#cite_note-44">[39]</a></sup> During the <a href="/wiki/Iron_Age" title="Iron Age">Iron Age</a>, the land was inhabited by <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Iranian_languages" title="Eastern Iranian languages">Iranian</a>-speaking <a href="/wiki/Cimmerians" title="Cimmerians">Cimmerians</a>, <a href="/wiki/Scythians" title="Scythians">Scythians</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Sarmatians" title="Sarmatians">Sarmatians</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-45"><a href="#cite_note-45">[40]</a></sup> Between 700 BC and 200 BC it was part of the <a href="/wiki/Scythia" title="Scythia">Scythian</a> kingdom.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-46"><a href="#cite_note-46">[41]</a></sup>
</p><p>From the 6th century BC, <a href="/wiki/Ancient_Greece" title="Ancient Greece">Greek</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ancient_Rome" title="Ancient Rome">Roman</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Byzantine_Empire" title="Byzantine Empire">Byzantine</a> colonies were established on the north-eastern shore of the <a href="/wiki/Black_Sea" title="Black Sea">Black Sea</a>, such as at <a href="/wiki/Tyras" title="Tyras">Tyras</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Olbia,_Ukraine" title="Olbia, Ukraine">Olbia</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Chersonesus" title="Chersonesus">Chersonesus</a>. These thrived into the 6th century AD. The <a href="/wiki/Goths" title="Goths">Goths</a> stayed in the area, but came under the sway of the <a href="/wiki/Huns" title="Huns">Huns</a> from the 370s. In the 7th century, the territory that is now eastern Ukraine was the centre of <a href="/wiki/Old_Great_Bulgaria" title="Old Great Bulgaria">Old Great Bulgaria</a>. At the end of the century, the majority of Bulgar tribes migrated in different directions, and the <a href="/wiki/Khazars" title="Khazars">Khazars</a> took over much of the land.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-47"><a href="#cite_note-47">[42]</a></sup>
</p><p>In the 5th and 6th centuries, the <a href="/wiki/Early_Slavs" title="Early Slavs">Early Slavic</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Antes_(people)" title="Antes (people)">Antes people</a> lived in Ukraine. The Antes were the ancestors of <a href="/wiki/Ukrainians" title="Ukrainians">Ukrainians</a>: <a href="/wiki/White_Croats" title="White Croats">White Croats</a>, <a href="/wiki/Severians" title="Severians">Severians</a>, <a href="/wiki/Polans_(eastern)" title="Polans (eastern)">Eastern Polans</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Drevlyans" title="Drevlyans">Drevlyans</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dulebes" title="Dulebes">Dulebes</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ulichians" title="Ulichians">Ulichians</a>, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tiverians" title="Tiverians">Tiverians</a>. Migrations from the territories of present-day Ukraine throughout the <a href="/wiki/Balkans" title="Balkans">Balkans</a> established many <a href="/wiki/South_Slavs" title="South Slavs">South Slavic</a> nations. Northern migrations, reaching almost to <a href="/wiki/Lake_Ilmen" title="Lake Ilmen">Lake Ilmen</a>, led to the emergence of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ilmen_Slavs" title="Ilmen Slavs">Ilmen Slavs</a>, <a href="/wiki/Krivichs" title="Krivichs">Krivichs</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Radimichs" title="Radimichs">Radimichs</a>, the groups ancestral to the <a href="/wiki/Russians" title="Russians">Russians</a>. Following an <a href="/wiki/Pannonian_Avars" title="Pannonian Avars">Avar</a> raid in 602 and the collapse of the Antes Union, most of these peoples survived as separate tribes until the beginning of the second millennium.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-48"><a href="#cite_note-48">[43]</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability"><span title="Quotation needed from source to verify. (March 2022)">need quotation to verify</span></a></i>]</sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Golden_Age_of_Kyiv">Golden Age of Kyiv</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Kievan_Rus%27" title="Kievan Rus'">Kievan Rus'</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Ruthenia" title="Kingdom of Ruthenia">Kingdom of Ruthenia</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:262px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Principalities_of_Kievan_Rus%27_(1054-1132).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1028" data-file-width="770" decoding="async" height="347" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/db/Principalities_of_Kievan_Rus%27_%281054-1132%29.jpg/260px-Principalities_of_Kievan_Rus%27_%281054-1132%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/db/Principalities_of_Kievan_Rus%27_%281054-1132%29.jpg/390px-Principalities_of_Kievan_Rus%27_%281054-1132%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/db/Principalities_of_Kievan_Rus%27_%281054-1132%29.jpg/520px-Principalities_of_Kievan_Rus%27_%281054-1132%29.jpg 2x" width="260"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Principalities_of_Kievan_Rus%27_(1054-1132).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The furthest extent of <a href="/wiki/Kievan_Rus%27" title="Kievan Rus'">Kievan Rus'</a>, 1054–1132</div></div></div>
<p>The establishment of the <a href="/wiki/Kievan_Rus%27" title="Kievan Rus'">Kievan Rus'</a> remains obscure and uncertain; there are at least three versions depending on interpretations of the chronicles.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-49"><a href="#cite_note-49">[44]</a></sup> In general, the state included much of present-day Ukraine, <a href="/wiki/Belarus" title="Belarus">Belarus</a> and the western part of <a href="/wiki/European_Russia" title="European Russia">European Russia</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Columbia_50-0"><a href="#cite_note-Columbia-50">[45]</a></sup> According to the <i><a href="/wiki/Primary_Chronicle" title="Primary Chronicle">Primary Chronicle</a></i> the Rus' elite and rulers initially consisted of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Varangian" title="Varangian">Varangians</a> from <a href="/wiki/Scandinavia" title="Scandinavia">Scandinavia</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-51"><a href="#cite_note-51">[46]</a></sup> In 882, the pagan <a href="/wiki/Oleg_of_Novgorod" title="Oleg of Novgorod">Prince Oleg</a> (Oleh) conquered <a href="/wiki/Kyiv" title="Kyiv">Kyiv</a> from <a href="/wiki/Askold_and_Dir" title="Askold and Dir">Askold and Dir</a> and proclaimed it as the capital of the Rus'.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-52"><a href="#cite_note-52">[47]</a></sup> However, it is also believed that the East Slavic tribes along the southern parts of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dnieper_River" title="Dnieper River">Dnieper River</a> were already in the process of forming a state independently.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-53"><a href="#cite_note-53">[48]</a></sup> In any case, the Varangians later assimilated into the Slavic population and became part of the first Rus' dynasty, the <a href="/wiki/Rurik_dynasty" title="Rurik dynasty">Rurik dynasty</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Columbia_50-1"><a href="#cite_note-Columbia-50">[45]</a></sup> Kievan Rus' was composed of several <a href="/wiki/Principality" title="Principality">principalities</a> ruled by the interrelated Rurikid <i><a href="/wiki/Knyaz" title="Knyaz">kniazes</a></i> ("princes"), who often fought each other for possession of Kyiv.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-54"><a href="#cite_note-54">[49]</a></sup>
</p><p>During the 10th and 11th centuries, Kievan Rus' became the largest and most powerful state in Europe, a period known as its Golden Age.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cia_55-0"><a href="#cite_note-cia-55">[50]</a></sup> It began with the reign of <a href="/wiki/Vladimir_the_Great" title="Vladimir the Great">Vladimir the Great</a> (980–1015), who <a href="/wiki/Christianization_of_Kievan_Rus%27" title="Christianization of Kievan Rus'">turned Rus' toward Byzantine Christianity</a>. During the reign of his son, <a href="/wiki/Yaroslav_the_Wise" title="Yaroslav the Wise">Yaroslav the Wise</a> (1019–1054), Kievan Rus' reached the zenith of its cultural development and military power.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Columbia_50-2"><a href="#cite_note-Columbia-50">[45]</a></sup> The state soon fragmented as the relative importance of regional powers rose again. After a final resurgence under the rule of <a href="/wiki/Vladimir_II_Monomakh" title="Vladimir II Monomakh">Vladimir II Monomakh</a> (1113–1125) and his son <a href="/wiki/Mstislav_I_of_Kiev" title="Mstislav I of Kiev">Mstislav</a> (1125–1132), Kievan Rus' finally disintegrated into separate principalities following Mstislav's death, though ownership of Kyiv would still carry great prestige for decades.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-56"><a href="#cite_note-56">[51]</a></sup> In the 11th and 12th centuries, the nomadic confederacy of the <a href="/wiki/Turkic_languages" title="Turkic languages">Turkic</a>-speaking <a href="/wiki/Cumans" title="Cumans">Cumans</a> and <a href="/wiki/Kipchaks" title="Kipchaks">Kipchaks</a> was the dominant force in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pontic_steppe" title="Pontic steppe">Pontic steppe</a> north of the Black Sea.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-57"><a href="#cite_note-57">[52]</a></sup>
</p><p>The 13th-century <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mongol_invasion_of_Rus%27" title="Mongol invasion of Rus'">Mongol invasion</a> devastated Kievan Rus' and Kyiv was completely <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Siege_of_Kyiv_(1240)" title="Siege of Kyiv (1240)">destroyed in 1240</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-58"><a href="#cite_note-58">[53]</a></sup> On today's Ukrainian territory, the principalities of <a href="/wiki/Principality_of_Halych" title="Principality of Halych">Halych</a> and <a href="/wiki/Volhynia" title="Volhynia">Volodymyr-Volynskyi</a> arose, and were merged into the state of <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Galicia%E2%80%93Volhynia" title="Kingdom of Galicia–Volhynia">Galicia–Volhynia</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-59"><a href="#cite_note-59">[54]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Daniel_of_Galicia" title="Daniel of Galicia">Daniel of Galicia</a>, son of <a href="/wiki/Roman_the_Great" title="Roman the Great">Roman the Great</a>, re-united much of south-western Rus', including <a href="/wiki/Volhynia" title="Volhynia">Volhynia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Galicia_(Eastern_Europe)" title="Galicia (Eastern Europe)">Galicia</a> and the ancient capital of Kyiv. He was subsequently crowned by the <a href="/wiki/Pope" title="Pope">papal</a> <a href="/wiki/Archbishop" title="Archbishop">archbishop</a> as the first <a href="/wiki/Monarch" title="Monarch">king</a> of the newly created <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Ruthenia" title="Kingdom of Ruthenia">Kingdom of Ruthenia</a> in 1253.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-60"><a href="#cite_note-60">[55]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Foreign_domination">Foreign domination</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Grand_Duchy_of_Lithuania" title="Grand Duchy of Lithuania">Grand Duchy of Lithuania</a>, <a href="/wiki/Crown_of_the_Kingdom_of_Poland" title="Crown of the Kingdom of Poland">Crown of the Kingdom of Poland</a>, <a href="/wiki/Crimean_Khanate" title="Crimean Khanate">Crimean Khanate</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ottoman_Empire" title="Ottoman Empire">Ottoman Empire</a>, <a href="/wiki/Polish%E2%80%93Lithuanian_Commonwealth" title="Polish–Lithuanian Commonwealth">Polish–Lithuanian Commonwealth</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Russian_Empire" title="Russian Empire">Russian Empire</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:262px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Rzeczpospolita2nar.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2480" data-file-width="3507" decoding="async" height="184" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f0/Rzeczpospolita2nar.png/260px-Rzeczpospolita2nar.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f0/Rzeczpospolita2nar.png/390px-Rzeczpospolita2nar.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f0/Rzeczpospolita2nar.png/520px-Rzeczpospolita2nar.png 2x" width="260"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Rzeczpospolita2nar.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Polish%E2%80%93Lithuanian_Commonwealth" title="Polish–Lithuanian Commonwealth">Polish–Lithuanian Commonwealth</a> at its maximum extent in 1619. <a href="/wiki/Poland" title="Poland">Poland</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Crown_of_the_Kingdom_of_Poland" title="Crown of the Kingdom of Poland">Polish Crown</a> exercised power over much of Ukraine since <a href="/wiki/Union_of_Lublin" title="Union of Lublin">1569</a>.</div></div></div>
<p>In 1349, Ruthenia ceased to exist as an independent entity in the aftermath of the <a href="/wiki/Galicia%E2%80%93Volhynia_Wars" title="Galicia–Volhynia Wars">Galicia–Volhynia Wars</a>, with its lands partitioned between the <a href="/wiki/Poland" title="Poland">Kingdom of Poland</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Grand_Duchy_of_Lithuania" title="Grand Duchy of Lithuania">Grand Duchy of Lithuania</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rowell266_61-0"><a href="#cite_note-rowell266-61">[56]</a></sup> From the mid-13th century to the late 1400s the <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_Genoa" title="Republic of Genoa">Republic of Genoa</a> founded numerous colonies in the Black Sea region of modern Ukraine and transformed these into large commercial centers headed by the consul, a representative of the Republic.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-62"><a href="#cite_note-62">[57]</a></sup> In 1430, the region of <a href="/wiki/Podolia" title="Podolia">Podolia</a> was incorporated into Poland and Ukraine became increasingly settled by Polish colonisers.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-63"><a href="#cite_note-63">[58]</a></sup> In 1441, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Genghisid" title="Genghisid">Genghisid</a> prince <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Haci_I_Giray" title="Haci I Giray">Haci I Giray</a> founded the <a href="/wiki/Crimean_Khanate" title="Crimean Khanate">Crimean Khanate</a> on the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Crimean_Peninsula" title="Crimean Peninsula">Crimean Peninsula</a> and the surrounding steppes;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-64"><a href="#cite_note-64">[59]</a></sup> the Khanate orchestrated <a href="/wiki/Tatars" title="Tatars">Tatar</a> <a href="/wiki/Crimean%E2%80%93Nogai_slave_raids_in_Eastern_Europe" title="Crimean–Nogai slave raids in Eastern Europe">slave raids</a> and took an estimated two million Ruthenian slaves.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-65"><a href="#cite_note-65">[60]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-66"><a href="#cite_note-66">[61]</a></sup>
</p><p>In 1569 the <a href="/wiki/Union_of_Lublin" title="Union of Lublin">Union of Lublin</a> established the <a href="/wiki/Polish%E2%80%93Lithuanian_Commonwealth" title="Polish–Lithuanian Commonwealth">Polish–Lithuanian Commonwealth</a>, and most of the former Ruthenian lands were transferred from Lithuania to the <a href="/wiki/Crown_of_the_Kingdom_of_Poland" title="Crown of the Kingdom of Poland">Crown of the Kingdom of Poland</a>, becoming <i><a href="/wiki/De_jure" title="De jure">de jure</a></i> Polish territory. Under the pressures of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Polonisation" title="Polonisation">Polonisation</a>, many landed gentry of <a href="/wiki/Ruthenia" title="Ruthenia">Ruthenia</a> converted to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Roman_Catholicism" title="Roman Catholicism">Catholicism</a> and joined the circles of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Polish_nobility" title="Polish nobility">Polish nobility</a>; others still joined the newly created <a href="/wiki/Ruthenian_Uniate_Church" title="Ruthenian Uniate Church">Ruthenian Uniate Church</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-67"><a href="#cite_note-67">[62]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Cossack_Hetmanate">Cossack Hetmanate</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Cossack_Hetmanate" title="Cossack Hetmanate">Cossack Hetmanate</a></div><p>Deprived of native protectors among Rus nobility, the peasants and townspeople began turning for protection to the emerging <a href="/wiki/Zaporozhian_Cossacks" title="Zaporozhian Cossacks">Zaporozhian Cossacks</a>. In the mid-17th century, a Cossack military quasi-state, the <a href="/wiki/Zaporozhian_Host" title="Zaporozhian Host">Zaporozhian Host</a>, was formed by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dnieper_Cossacks" title="Dnieper Cossacks">Dnieper Cossacks</a> and Ruthenian peasants.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-zaporizhia_68-0"><a href="#cite_note-zaporizhia-68">[63]</a></sup> Poland exercised little real control over this population, but found the Cossacks to be useful against the <a href="/wiki/Ottoman_Empire" title="Ottoman Empire">Turks</a> and <a href="/wiki/Crimean_Khanate" title="Crimean Khanate">Tatars</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-britcos_69-0"><a href="#cite_note-britcos-69">[64]</a></sup> and at times the two were allies in <a href="/wiki/Ottoman_wars_in_Europe" title="Ottoman wars in Europe">military campaigns</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-70"><a href="#cite_note-70">[65]</a></sup> However, the continued harsh <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Serf" title="Serf">enserfment</a> of Ruthenian peasantry by Polish overlords and the suppression of the Orthodox Church alienated the Cossacks.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-britcos_69-1"><a href="#cite_note-britcos-69">[64]</a></sup> The latter did not shy from taking up arms against those they perceived as enemies and occupiers, including the Polish Catholic state with its local representatives.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-71"><a href="#cite_note-71">[66]</a></sup></p><div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Hondius_Bohdan_Khmelnytsky.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1662" data-file-width="1116" decoding="async" height="253" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/33/Hondius_Bohdan_Khmelnytsky.jpg/170px-Hondius_Bohdan_Khmelnytsky.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/33/Hondius_Bohdan_Khmelnytsky.jpg/255px-Hondius_Bohdan_Khmelnytsky.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/33/Hondius_Bohdan_Khmelnytsky.jpg/340px-Hondius_Bohdan_Khmelnytsky.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Hondius_Bohdan_Khmelnytsky.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Hetmans_of_Ukrainian_Cossacks" title="Hetmans of Ukrainian Cossacks">Hetman</a> <a href="/wiki/Bohdan_Khmelnytsky" title="Bohdan Khmelnytsky">Bohdan Khmelnytsky</a> established an independent <a href="/wiki/Cossack_Hetmanate" title="Cossack Hetmanate">Cossack state</a> after the <a href="/wiki/Khmelnytsky_Uprising" title="Khmelnytsky Uprising">1648 uprising</a> against Poland.</div></div></div>
<p>In 1648, <a href="/wiki/Bohdan_Khmelnytsky" title="Bohdan Khmelnytsky">Bohdan Khmelnytsky</a> led the <a href="/wiki/Khmelnytsky_Uprising" title="Khmelnytsky Uprising">largest of the Cossack uprisings</a> against the Commonwealth and the <a href="/wiki/List_of_Polish_monarchs" title="List of Polish monarchs">Polish king</a>, which enjoyed wide support from the local population.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-72"><a href="#cite_note-72">[67]</a></sup> Khmelnytsky founded the <a href="/wiki/Cossack_Hetmanate" title="Cossack Hetmanate">Cossack Hetmanate</a>, which existed until 1764 (some sources claim until 1782).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-73"><a href="#cite_note-73">[68]</a></sup> After Khmelnytsky suffered a crushing defeat at the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Berestechko" title="Battle of Berestechko">Battle of Berestechko</a> in 1651, he turned to the <a href="/wiki/List_of_Russian_monarchs" title="List of Russian monarchs">Russian tsar</a> for help. In 1654, Khmelnytsky was subject to the <a href="/wiki/Pereiaslav_Agreement" title="Pereiaslav Agreement">Pereiaslav Agreement</a>, forming a military and political alliance with Russia that acknowledged loyalty to the Russian monarch.
</p><p>After his death, the Hetmanate went through a devastating 30-year war amongst Russia, Poland, the <a href="/wiki/Crimean_Khanate" title="Crimean Khanate">Crimean Khanate</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Ottoman_Empire" title="Ottoman Empire">Ottoman Empire</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Cossacks" title="Cossacks">Cossacks</a>, known as "<a href="/wiki/The_Ruin_(Ukrainian_history)" title="The Ruin (Ukrainian history)">The Ruin</a>" (1657-1686), for control of the Cossack Hetmanate. The "<a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Perpetual_Peace_(1686)" title="Treaty of Perpetual Peace (1686)">Treaty of Perpetual Peace</a>" between Russia and Poland in 1686 divided the lands of the Cossack Hetmanate between them, reducing the portion over which Poland had claimed sovereignty to Ukraine west of the <a href="/wiki/Dnieper" title="Dnieper">Dnieper</a> river. In 1686, the <a href="/wiki/Metropolitanate_of_Kyiv" title="Metropolitanate of Kyiv">Metropolitanate of Kyiv</a> was <a href="/wiki/Annexation_of_the_Metropolitanate_of_Kyiv_by_the_Moscow_Patriarchate" title="Annexation of the Metropolitanate of Kyiv by the Moscow Patriarchate">annexed by the Moscow Patriarchate</a> through a synodal letter of the <a href="/wiki/Ecumenical_Patriarch_of_Constantinople" title="Ecumenical Patriarch of Constantinople">Ecumenical Patriarch of Constantinople</a> <a href="/wiki/Dionysius_IV_of_Constantinople" title="Dionysius IV of Constantinople">Dionysius IV</a>, thus placing the <a href="/wiki/Metropolitanate_of_Kyiv#Orthodox_Church_of_Ukraine" title="Metropolitanate of Kyiv">Metropolitanate of Kyiv</a> under the authority of <a href="/wiki/Moscow" title="Moscow">Moscow</a>. An attempt to reverse the decline was undertaken by Cossack Hetman <a href="/wiki/Ivan_Mazepa" title="Ivan Mazepa">Ivan Mazepa</a> (1639–1709), who ultimately defected to the <a href="/wiki/Sweden" title="Sweden">Swedes</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Great_Northern_War" title="Great Northern War">Great Northern War</a> (1700-1721) in a bid to get rid of Russian dependence,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Magocsi_74-0"><a href="#cite_note-Magocsi-74">[69]</a></sup> but they were crushed in the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Poltava" title="Battle of Poltava">Battle of Poltava</a> (1709).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Magocsi_74-1"><a href="#cite_note-Magocsi-74">[69]</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Battle_of_Poltava_1709.PNG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="817" data-file-width="1424" decoding="async" height="126" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/88/Battle_of_Poltava_1709.PNG/220px-Battle_of_Poltava_1709.PNG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/88/Battle_of_Poltava_1709.PNG/330px-Battle_of_Poltava_1709.PNG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/88/Battle_of_Poltava_1709.PNG/440px-Battle_of_Poltava_1709.PNG 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Battle_of_Poltava_1709.PNG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Russia's victory over <a href="/wiki/Charles_XII_of_Sweden" title="Charles XII of Sweden">Charles XII of Sweden</a> and his ally <a href="/wiki/Ivan_Mazepa" title="Ivan Mazepa">Ivan Mazepa</a> at the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Poltava" title="Battle of Poltava">Battle of Poltava</a> (1709) destroyed <a href="/wiki/Cossacks" title="Cossacks">Cossack</a> autonomy.</div></div></div>
<p>The Hetmanate's autonomy was severely restricted since Poltava. In the years 1764–1781, <a href="/wiki/Catherine_the_Great" title="Catherine the Great">Catherine the Great</a> incorporated much of <a href="/wiki/Central_Ukraine" title="Central Ukraine">Central Ukraine</a> into the <a href="/wiki/Russian_Empire" title="Russian Empire">Russian Empire</a>, abolishing the <a href="/wiki/Cossack_Hetmanate" title="Cossack Hetmanate">Cossack Hetmanate</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Zaporozhian_Sich" title="Zaporozhian Sich">Zaporozhian Sich</a>, and was one of the people responsible for the suppression of the last major Cossack uprising, the <a href="/wiki/Koliivshchyna" title="Koliivshchyna">Koliivshchyna</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-75"><a href="#cite_note-75">[70]</a></sup> After the <a href="/wiki/Annexation_of_Crimea_by_the_Russian_Empire" title="Annexation of Crimea by the Russian Empire">annexation of Crimea by Russia</a> in 1783, the newly acquired lands, now called <a href="/wiki/Novorossiya" title="Novorossiya">Novorossiya</a>, were opened up to settlement by Russians.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-76"><a href="#cite_note-76">[71]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Tsarist_autocracy" title="Tsarist autocracy">tsarist autocracy</a> established a policy of <a href="/wiki/Russification" title="Russification">Russification</a>, suppressing the use of the <a href="/wiki/Ukrainian_language" title="Ukrainian language">Ukrainian language</a> and curtailing the Ukrainian national identity.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-censor_77-0"><a href="#cite_note-censor-77">[72]</a></sup> The western part of present-day Ukraine was subsequently split between Russia and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Habsburg" title="Habsburg">Habsburg</a>-ruled <a href="/wiki/Austrian_Empire" title="Austrian Empire">Austria</a> after the <a href="/wiki/Partitions_of_Poland" title="Partitions of Poland">fall</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Polish%E2%80%93Lithuanian_Commonwealth" title="Polish–Lithuanian Commonwealth">Polish–Lithuanian Commonwealth</a> in 1795.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="19th_and_early_20th_century">19th and early 20th century</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Southwestern_Krai" title="Southwestern Krai">Southwestern Krai</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kharkov_Governorate" title="Kharkov Governorate">Kharkov Governorate</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Chernigov_Governorate" title="Chernigov Governorate">Chernigov Governorate</a></div>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Ukraine_during_World_War_I" title="Ukraine during World War I">Ukraine during World War I</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ukraine_after_the_Russian_Revolution" title="Ukraine after the Russian Revolution">Ukraine after the Russian Revolution</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ukrainian_War_of_Independence" title="Ukrainian War of Independence">Ukrainian War of Independence</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Ukrainian%E2%80%93Soviet_War" title="Ukrainian–Soviet War">Ukrainian–Soviet War</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Polish_troops_in_Kiev.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="873" data-file-width="1200" decoding="async" height="160" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4a/Polish_troops_in_Kiev.jpg/220px-Polish_troops_in_Kiev.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4a/Polish_troops_in_Kiev.jpg/330px-Polish_troops_in_Kiev.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4a/Polish_troops_in_Kiev.jpg/440px-Polish_troops_in_Kiev.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Polish_troops_in_Kiev.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Kiev_Offensive_(1920)" title="Kiev Offensive (1920)">Polish troops enter Kyiv</a> in May 1920 during the <a href="/wiki/Polish%E2%80%93Soviet_War" title="Polish–Soviet War">Polish–Soviet War</a>. Following the <a href="/wiki/Peace_of_Riga" title="Peace of Riga">Peace of Riga</a> signed on 18 March 1921, Poland took control of modern-day western Ukraine while Soviets took control of eastern and central Ukraine.</div></div></div>
<p>The 19th century saw the rise of Ukrainian nationalism. With growing urbanization and modernization and a cultural trend toward <a href="/wiki/Romantic_nationalism" title="Romantic nationalism">romantic nationalism</a>, the Ukrainian <a href="/wiki/Intelligentsia" title="Intelligentsia">intelligentsia</a> committed to national rebirth and social justice emerged. The serf-turned-national-poet <a href="/wiki/Taras_Shevchenko" title="Taras Shevchenko">Taras Shevchenko</a> (1814–1861) and political theorist <a href="/wiki/Mykhailo_Drahomanov" title="Mykhailo Drahomanov">Mykhailo Drahomanov</a> (1841–1895) led the growing nationalist movement.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-78"><a href="#cite_note-78">[73]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-79"><a href="#cite_note-79">[74]</a></sup> While conditions for its development in Austrian <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Galicia_(eastern_Europe)" title="Galicia (eastern Europe)">Galicia</a> under the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Habsburgs" title="Habsburgs">Habsburgs</a> were relatively lenient,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-80"><a href="#cite_note-80">[75]</a></sup> the Russian part (known as <a href="/wiki/Little_Russia" title="Little Russia">Little Russia</a>) faced severe restrictions, going as far as <a href="/wiki/Ems_Ukaz" title="Ems Ukaz">banning virtually all books from being published in Ukrainian</a> in 1876.
</p><p>Ukraine joined the <a href="/wiki/Industrial_Revolution" title="Industrial Revolution">Industrial Revolution</a> <a href="/wiki/Industrialization_in_the_Russian_Empire" title="Industrialization in the Russian Empire">later</a> than most of Western Europe<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-81"><a href="#cite_note-81">[76]</a></sup> due to the maintenance of <a href="/wiki/Serfdom_in_Russia" title="Serfdom in Russia">serfdom</a> until 1861. Other than near the newly discovered coal fields of the <a href="/wiki/Donbas" title="Donbas">Donbas</a>, and in some larger cities such as <a href="/wiki/Odesa" title="Odesa">Odesa</a> and Kyiv, Ukraine largely remained an agricultural and resource extraction economy.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-82"><a href="#cite_note-82">[77]</a></sup> The Austrian part of Ukraine <a href="/wiki/Poverty_in_Austrian_Galicia" title="Poverty in Austrian Galicia">was particularly destitute</a>, which forced hundreds of thousands of peasants into emigration, who created the backbone of an extensive <a href="/wiki/Ukrainian_diaspora" title="Ukrainian diaspora">Ukrainian diaspora</a> in countries such as <a href="/wiki/Ukrainian_Canadians" title="Ukrainian Canadians">Canada</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Ukrainian_Americans" title="Ukrainian Americans">United States</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ukrainian_Brazilians" title="Ukrainian Brazilians">Brazil</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-83"><a href="#cite_note-83">[78]</a></sup> Some of the Ukrainians settled in the Far East, too. According to the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/1897_census" title="1897 census">1897 census</a>, there were 223,000 ethnic Ukrainians in <a href="/wiki/Siberia" title="Siberia">Siberia</a> and 102,000 in <a href="/wiki/Central_Asia" title="Central Asia">Central Asia</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-84"><a href="#cite_note-84">[79]</a></sup> An additional 1.6 million emigrated to the east in the ten years after the opening of the <a href="/wiki/Trans-Siberian_Railway" title="Trans-Siberian Railway">Trans-Siberian Railway</a> in 1906.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-85"><a href="#cite_note-85">[80]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Russian_Far_East" title="Russian Far East">Far Eastern</a> areas with an ethnic Ukrainian population became known as <a href="/wiki/Green_Ukraine" title="Green Ukraine">Green Ukraine</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-86"><a href="#cite_note-86">[81]</a></sup>
</p><p>Ukraine plunged into turmoil with the beginning of <a href="/wiki/World_War_I" title="World War I">World War I</a>, and fighting on Ukrainian soil persisted until late 1921. Initially, the Ukrainians were split between Austria-Hungary, fighting for the <a href="/wiki/Central_Powers" title="Central Powers">Central Powers</a>, though the vast majority served in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Military_history_of_Imperial_Russia" title="Military history of Imperial Russia">Imperial Russian Army</a>, which was part of the <a href="/wiki/Triple_Entente" title="Triple Entente">Triple Entente</a>, under Russia.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-87"><a href="#cite_note-87">[82]</a></sup> As the Russian Empire collapsed, the conflict evolved into the <a href="/wiki/Ukrainian_War_of_Independence" title="Ukrainian War of Independence">Ukrainian War of Independence</a>, with Ukrainians fighting alongside, or against, the <a href="/wiki/Red_Army" title="Red Army">Red</a>, <a href="/wiki/White_Army" title="White Army">White</a>, <a href="/wiki/Makhnovshchina" title="Makhnovshchina">Black</a> and <a href="/wiki/Green_armies" title="Green armies">Green armies</a>, with the Poles, (in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Transcarpathian_Rus%27" title="Transcarpathian Rus'">Transcarpathia</a>) Hungarians, and Germans also intervening at various times.
</p><p>An attempt to create an independent state, the left-leaning <a href="/wiki/Ukrainian_People%27s_Republic" title="Ukrainian People's Republic">Ukrainian People's Republic</a> (UNR), was first announced by <a href="/wiki/Mykhailo_Hrushevsky" title="Mykhailo Hrushevsky">Mykhailo Hrushevsky</a>, but the period was plagued by an extremely unstable political and military environment. It was first deposed in a <a href="/wiki/Coup_d%27%C3%A9tat" title="Coup d'état">coup d'état</a> led by <a href="/wiki/Pavlo_Skoropadskyi" title="Pavlo Skoropadskyi">Pavlo Skoropadskyi</a>, which yielded the <a href="/wiki/Ukrainian_State" title="Ukrainian State">Ukrainian State</a> under the German protectorate, and the attempt to restore the UNR under the <a href="/wiki/Directorate_of_Ukraine" title="Directorate of Ukraine">Directorate</a> ultimately failed as the Ukrainian army was regularly overrun by other forces. The short-lived <a href="/wiki/West_Ukrainian_People%27s_Republic" title="West Ukrainian People's Republic">West Ukrainian People's Republic</a> and <a href="/wiki/Hutsul_Republic" title="Hutsul Republic">Hutsul Republic</a> also failed to join the rest of Ukraine.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-88"><a href="#cite_note-88">[83]</a></sup>
</p><p>The result of the conflict was a partial victory for the <a href="/wiki/Second_Polish_Republic" title="Second Polish Republic">Second Polish Republic</a>, which annexed the Western Ukrainian provinces, as well as a larger-scale victory for the pro-Soviet forces, which succeeded in dislodging the remaining factions and eventually established the <a href="/wiki/Ukrainian_Soviet_Socialist_Republic" title="Ukrainian Soviet Socialist Republic">Ukrainian Soviet Socialist Republic</a> (Soviet Ukraine). Meanwhile, modern-day <a href="/wiki/Bukovina" title="Bukovina">Bukovina</a> was occupied by <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Romania" title="Kingdom of Romania">Romania</a> and <a href="/wiki/Carpathian_Ruthenia" title="Carpathian Ruthenia">Carpathian Ruthenia</a> was admitted to <a href="/wiki/First_Czechoslovak_Republic" title="First Czechoslovak Republic">Czechoslovakia</a> as an autonomous region.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-89"><a href="#cite_note-89">[84]</a></sup>
</p><p>The conflict over Ukraine, a part of the broader <a href="/wiki/Russian_Civil_War" title="Russian Civil War">Russian Civil War</a>, devastated the whole of the former <a href="/wiki/Russian_Empire" title="Russian Empire">Russian Empire</a>, including eastern and central Ukraine. The fighting left over 1.5 million people dead and hundreds of thousands homeless in the former Russian Empire's territory. The eastern provinces were additionally impacted by a <a href="/wiki/Russian_famine_of_1921%E2%80%931922" title="Russian famine of 1921–1922">famine in 1921</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-90"><a href="#cite_note-90">[85]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-91"><a href="#cite_note-91">[86]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Inter-war_Ukraine">Inter-war Ukraine</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Holodomor" title="Holodomor">Holodomor</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:GolodomorKharkiv.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1191" data-file-width="1600" decoding="async" height="164" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a3/GolodomorKharkiv.jpg/220px-GolodomorKharkiv.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a3/GolodomorKharkiv.jpg/330px-GolodomorKharkiv.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a3/GolodomorKharkiv.jpg/440px-GolodomorKharkiv.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:GolodomorKharkiv.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Starved peasants on a street in <a href="/wiki/Kharkiv" title="Kharkiv">Kharkiv</a>, 1933. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Collectivization" title="Collectivization">Collectivization</a> of crops and their confiscation by Soviet authorities led to a major famine in Soviet Ukraine known as the <a href="/wiki/Holodomor" title="Holodomor">Holodomor</a>.</div></div></div>
<p>In <a href="/wiki/Second_Polish_Republic" title="Second Polish Republic">Poland</a>, the government openly propagated <a href="/wiki/Anti-Ukrainian_sentiment" title="Anti-Ukrainian sentiment">anti-Ukrainian sentiment</a> and restricted rights of people who declared Ukrainian nationality and belonged to the <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Orthodox_Church" title="Eastern Orthodox Church">Eastern Orthodox Church</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-auto2_92-0"><a href="#cite_note-auto2-92">[87]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-auto3_93-0"><a href="#cite_note-auto3-93">[88]</a></sup> In consequence, an underground Ukrainian nationalist and militant movement arose in the 1920s and 1930s, which gradually transformed into the <a href="/wiki/Ukrainian_Military_Organization" title="Ukrainian Military Organization">Ukrainian Military Organization</a> and later the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Organisation_of_Ukrainian_Nationalists" title="Organisation of Ukrainian Nationalists">Organisation of Ukrainian Nationalists</a> (OUN).
</p><p>Meanwhile, the recently constituted Soviet Ukraine became one of the founding republics of the <a href="/wiki/Soviet_Union" title="Soviet Union">Soviet Union</a>. During the 1920s,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-94"><a href="#cite_note-94">[89]</a></sup> under the Ukrainisation policy pursued by the national Communist leadership of <a href="/wiki/Mykola_Skrypnyk" title="Mykola Skrypnyk">Mykola Skrypnyk</a>, Soviet leadership at first encouraged a national renaissance in <a href="/wiki/Culture_of_Ukraine" title="Culture of Ukraine">Ukrainian culture</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ukrainian_language" title="Ukrainian language">language</a>. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ukrainisation" title="Ukrainisation">Ukrainisation</a> was part of the Soviet-wide policy of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Korenisation" title="Korenisation">Korenisation</a> (literally <i>indigenisation</i>), which was intended to promote the advancement of native peoples, their language and culture into the governance of their respective republics.
</p><p>Around the same time, Soviet leader <a href="/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin" title="Vladimir Lenin">Vladimir Lenin</a> instituted the <a href="/wiki/New_Economic_Policy" title="New Economic Policy">New Economic Policy</a> (NEP), which introduced a form of <a href="/wiki/Market_socialism" title="Market socialism">market socialism</a>, allowing some private ownership of small and medium-sized productive enterprises, hoping to reconstruct the post-war Soviet Union that had been devastated by both WWI and later the civil war. The NEP was successful at restoring the formerly war-torn nation to pre-WWI levels of production and agricultural output by the mid-1920s, much of the latter based in Ukraine.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Service_95-0"><a href="#cite_note-Service-95">[90]</a></sup> These policies attracted many prominent former UNR figures, including former UNR leader Hrushevsky, to return to Soviet Ukraine, where they were accepted, and participated in the advancement of Ukrainian science and culture.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-96"><a href="#cite_note-96">[91]</a></sup>
</p><p>This period was cut short when <a href="/wiki/Joseph_Stalin" title="Joseph Stalin">Joseph Stalin</a> became the leader of the USSR following Lenin's death. Stalin did away with the NEP in what became known as the <a href="/wiki/Great_Break_(USSR)" title="Great Break (USSR)">Great Break</a>. Starting from the late 1920s and now with a <a href="/wiki/Planned_economy" title="Planned economy">centrally planned economy</a>, Soviet Ukraine took part in an <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Industrialization_in_the_USSR" title="Industrialization in the USSR">industrialisation scheme</a> which quadrupled its industrial output during the 1930s.
</p><p>However, as a consequence of Stalin's new policy, the Ukrainian peasantry suffered from the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Collectivization_in_the_USSR" title="Collectivization in the USSR">programme of collectivization</a> of agricultural crops. Collectivization was part of the <a href="/wiki/First_five-year_plan" title="First five-year plan">first five-year plan</a> and was enforced by regular troops and the secret police known as <a href="/wiki/Cheka" title="Cheka">Cheka</a>. Those who resisted were <a href="/wiki/Population_transfer_in_the_Soviet_Union" title="Population transfer in the Soviet Union">arrested and deported</a> to <a href="/wiki/Gulag" title="Gulag">gulags</a> and work camps. As members of the collective farms were sometimes not allowed to receive any grain until unrealistic quotas were met, millions starved to death in a <a href="/wiki/Droughts_and_famines_in_Russia_and_the_Soviet_Union" title="Droughts and famines in Russia and the Soviet Union">famine</a> known as the <a href="/wiki/Holodomor" title="Holodomor">Holodomor</a> or the "Great Famine", which was recognized by some countries as an act of <a href="/wiki/Genocide" title="Genocide">genocide</a> perpetrated by <a href="/wiki/Joseph_Stalin" title="Joseph Stalin">Joseph Stalin</a> and other Soviet notables.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-97"><a href="#cite_note-97">[92]</a></sup>
</p><p>Following on the Russian Civil War, and collectivisation, the <a href="/wiki/Great_Purge" title="Great Purge">Great Purge</a>, while killing Stalin's perceived political enemies, resulted in a profound loss of a new generation of Ukrainian <a href="/wiki/Intelligentsia" title="Intelligentsia">intelligentsia</a>, known today as the <a href="/wiki/Executed_Renaissance" title="Executed Renaissance">Executed Renaissance</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-98"><a href="#cite_note-98">[93]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="World_War_II">World War II</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Front_(World_War_II)" title="Eastern Front (World War II)">Eastern Front (World War II)</a>, <a href="/wiki/Reichskommissariat_Ukraine" title="Reichskommissariat Ukraine">Reichskommissariat Ukraine</a>, and <a href="/wiki/The_Holocaust_in_Ukraine" title="The Holocaust in Ukraine">The Holocaust in Ukraine</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Ukraine-growth.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="475" data-file-width="800" decoding="async" height="178" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/07/Ukraine-growth.png/300px-Ukraine-growth.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/07/Ukraine-growth.png/450px-Ukraine-growth.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/07/Ukraine-growth.png/600px-Ukraine-growth.png 2x" width="300"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Ukraine-growth.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Territorial evolution of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ukrainian_SSR" title="Ukrainian SSR">Ukrainian SSR</a>, 1922–1954</div></div></div>
<p>Following the <a href="/wiki/Invasion_of_Poland" title="Invasion of Poland">Invasion of Poland</a> in September 1939, <a href="/wiki/Nazi_Germany" title="Nazi Germany">German</a> and <a href="/wiki/Soviet_Army" title="Soviet Army">Soviet</a> troops divided the territory of Poland. Thus, Eastern <a href="/wiki/Galicia_(Eastern_Europe)" title="Galicia (Eastern Europe)">Galicia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Volhynia" title="Volhynia">Volhynia</a> with their Ukrainian population became part of Ukraine. For the first time in history, the nation was united.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-99"><a href="#cite_note-99">[94]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-100"><a href="#cite_note-100">[95]</a></sup> Further territorial gains were secured in 1940, when the Ukrainian SSR incorporated the northern and southern districts of <a href="/wiki/Bessarabia" title="Bessarabia">Bessarabia</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Northern_Bukovina" title="Northern Bukovina">Northern Bukovina</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Hertsa_region" title="Hertsa region">Hertsa region</a> from the territories the USSR <a href="/wiki/Soviet_occupation_of_Bessarabia_and_Northern_Bukovina" title="Soviet occupation of Bessarabia and Northern Bukovina">forced Romania to cede</a>, though it handed over the western part of the <a href="/wiki/Moldavian_Autonomous_Soviet_Socialist_Republic" title="Moldavian Autonomous Soviet Socialist Republic">Moldavian Autonomous Soviet Socialist Republic</a> to the newly created <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Moldavian_SSR" title="Moldavian SSR">Moldavian SSR</a>. These territorial gains of the USSR were internationally recognized by the <a href="/wiki/Paris_Peace_Treaties,_1947" title="Paris Peace Treaties, 1947">Paris peace treaties of 1947</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-101"><a href="#cite_note-101">[96]</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:182px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:%D0%9C%D0%B0%D1%80%D1%88%D0%B0%D0%BB_%D0%A1%D0%BE%D0%B2%D0%B5%D1%82%D1%81%D0%BA%D0%BE%D0%B3%D0%BE_%D0%A1%D0%BE%D1%8E%D0%B7%D0%B0_%D0%93%D0%B5%D1%80%D0%BE%D0%B9_%D0%A1%D0%BE%D0%B2%D0%B5%D1%82%D1%81%D0%BA%D0%BE%D0%B3%D0%BE_%D0%A1%D0%BE%D1%8E%D0%B7%D0%B0_%D0%A1%D0%B5%D0%BC%D1%91%D0%BD_%D0%9A%D0%BE%D0%BD%D1%81%D1%82%D0%B0%D0%BD%D1%82%D0%B8%D0%BD%D0%BE%D0%B2%D0%B8%D1%87_%D0%A2%D0%B8%D0%BC%D0%BE%D1%88%D0%B5%D0%BD%D0%BA%D0%BE.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2096" data-file-width="1553" decoding="async" height="243" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fe/%D0%9C%D0%B0%D1%80%D1%88%D0%B0%D0%BB_%D0%A1%D0%BE%D0%B2%D0%B5%D1%82%D1%81%D0%BA%D0%BE%D0%B3%D0%BE_%D0%A1%D0%BE%D1%8E%D0%B7%D0%B0_%D0%93%D0%B5%D1%80%D0%BE%D0%B9_%D0%A1%D0%BE%D0%B2%D0%B5%D1%82%D1%81%D0%BA%D0%BE%D0%B3%D0%BE_%D0%A1%D0%BE%D1%8E%D0%B7%D0%B0_%D0%A1%D0%B5%D0%BC%D1%91%D0%BD_%D0%9A%D0%BE%D0%BD%D1%81%D1%82%D0%B0%D0%BD%D1%82%D0%B8%D0%BD%D0%BE%D0%B2%D0%B8%D1%87_%D0%A2%D0%B8%D0%BC%D0%BE%D1%88%D0%B5%D0%BD%D0%BA%D0%BE.jpg/180px-%D0%9C%D0%B0%D1%80%D1%88%D0%B0%D0%BB_%D0%A1%D0%BE%D0%B2%D0%B5%D1%82%D1%81%D0%BA%D0%BE%D0%B3%D0%BE_%D0%A1%D0%BE%D1%8E%D0%B7%D0%B0_%D0%93%D0%B5%D1%80%D0%BE%D0%B9_%D0%A1%D0%BE%D0%B2%D0%B5%D1%82%D1%81%D0%BA%D0%BE%D0%B3%D0%BE_%D0%A1%D0%BE%D1%8E%D0%B7%D0%B0_%D0%A1%D0%B5%D0%BC%D1%91%D0%BD_%D0%9A%D0%BE%D0%BD%D1%81%D1%82%D0%B0%D0%BD%D1%82%D0%B8%D0%BD%D0%BE%D0%B2%D0%B8%D1%87_%D0%A2%D0%B8%D0%BC%D0%BE%D1%88%D0%B5%D0%BD%D0%BA%D0%BE.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fe/%D0%9C%D0%B0%D1%80%D1%88%D0%B0%D0%BB_%D0%A1%D0%BE%D0%B2%D0%B5%D1%82%D1%81%D0%BA%D0%BE%D0%B3%D0%BE_%D0%A1%D0%BE%D1%8E%D0%B7%D0%B0_%D0%93%D0%B5%D1%80%D0%BE%D0%B9_%D0%A1%D0%BE%D0%B2%D0%B5%D1%82%D1%81%D0%BA%D0%BE%D0%B3%D0%BE_%D0%A1%D0%BE%D1%8E%D0%B7%D0%B0_%D0%A1%D0%B5%D0%BC%D1%91%D0%BD_%D0%9A%D0%BE%D0%BD%D1%81%D1%82%D0%B0%D0%BD%D1%82%D0%B8%D0%BD%D0%BE%D0%B2%D0%B8%D1%87_%D0%A2%D0%B8%D0%BC%D0%BE%D1%88%D0%B5%D0%BD%D0%BA%D0%BE.jpg/270px-%D0%9C%D0%B0%D1%80%D1%88%D0%B0%D0%BB_%D0%A1%D0%BE%D0%B2%D0%B5%D1%82%D1%81%D0%BA%D0%BE%D0%B3%D0%BE_%D0%A1%D0%BE%D1%8E%D0%B7%D0%B0_%D0%93%D0%B5%D1%80%D0%BE%D0%B9_%D0%A1%D0%BE%D0%B2%D0%B5%D1%82%D1%81%D0%BA%D0%BE%D0%B3%D0%BE_%D0%A1%D0%BE%D1%8E%D0%B7%D0%B0_%D0%A1%D0%B5%D0%BC%D1%91%D0%BD_%D0%9A%D0%BE%D0%BD%D1%81%D1%82%D0%B0%D0%BD%D1%82%D0%B8%D0%BD%D0%BE%D0%B2%D0%B8%D1%87_%D0%A2%D0%B8%D0%BC%D0%BE%D1%88%D0%B5%D0%BD%D0%BA%D0%BE.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fe/%D0%9C%D0%B0%D1%80%D1%88%D0%B0%D0%BB_%D0%A1%D0%BE%D0%B2%D0%B5%D1%82%D1%81%D0%BA%D0%BE%D0%B3%D0%BE_%D0%A1%D0%BE%D1%8E%D0%B7%D0%B0_%D0%93%D0%B5%D1%80%D0%BE%D0%B9_%D0%A1%D0%BE%D0%B2%D0%B5%D1%82%D1%81%D0%BA%D0%BE%D0%B3%D0%BE_%D0%A1%D0%BE%D1%8E%D0%B7%D0%B0_%D0%A1%D0%B5%D0%BC%D1%91%D0%BD_%D0%9A%D0%BE%D0%BD%D1%81%D1%82%D0%B0%D0%BD%D1%82%D0%B8%D0%BD%D0%BE%D0%B2%D0%B8%D1%87_%D0%A2%D0%B8%D0%BC%D0%BE%D1%88%D0%B5%D0%BD%D0%BA%D0%BE.jpg/360px-%D0%9C%D0%B0%D1%80%D1%88%D0%B0%D0%BB_%D0%A1%D0%BE%D0%B2%D0%B5%D1%82%D1%81%D0%BA%D0%BE%D0%B3%D0%BE_%D0%A1%D0%BE%D1%8E%D0%B7%D0%B0_%D0%93%D0%B5%D1%80%D0%BE%D0%B9_%D0%A1%D0%BE%D0%B2%D0%B5%D1%82%D1%81%D0%BA%D0%BE%D0%B3%D0%BE_%D0%A1%D0%BE%D1%8E%D0%B7%D0%B0_%D0%A1%D0%B5%D0%BC%D1%91%D0%BD_%D0%9A%D0%BE%D0%BD%D1%81%D1%82%D0%B0%D0%BD%D1%82%D0%B8%D0%BD%D0%BE%D0%B2%D0%B8%D1%87_%D0%A2%D0%B8%D0%BC%D0%BE%D1%88%D0%B5%D0%BD%D0%BA%D0%BE.jpg 2x" width="180"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:%D0%9C%D0%B0%D1%80%D1%88%D0%B0%D0%BB_%D0%A1%D0%BE%D0%B2%D0%B5%D1%82%D1%81%D0%BA%D0%BE%D0%B3%D0%BE_%D0%A1%D0%BE%D1%8E%D0%B7%D0%B0_%D0%93%D0%B5%D1%80%D0%BE%D0%B9_%D0%A1%D0%BE%D0%B2%D0%B5%D1%82%D1%81%D0%BA%D0%BE%D0%B3%D0%BE_%D0%A1%D0%BE%D1%8E%D0%B7%D0%B0_%D0%A1%D0%B5%D0%BC%D1%91%D0%BD_%D0%9A%D0%BE%D0%BD%D1%81%D1%82%D0%B0%D0%BD%D1%82%D0%B8%D0%BD%D0%BE%D0%B2%D0%B8%D1%87_%D0%A2%D0%B8%D0%BC%D0%BE%D1%88%D0%B5%D0%BD%D0%BA%D0%BE.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Marshal <a href="/wiki/Semyon_Timoshenko" title="Semyon Timoshenko">Semyon Timoshenko</a> (born in the <a href="/wiki/Budjak" title="Budjak">Budjak</a> region) commanded numerous fronts throughout the war, including the <a href="/wiki/Southwestern_Front_(Soviet_Union)" title="Southwestern Front (Soviet Union)">Southwestern Front</a> east of Kyiv in 1941.</div></div></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Wehrmacht" title="Wehrmacht">German armies</a> <a href="/wiki/Operation_Barbarossa" title="Operation Barbarossa">invaded the Soviet Union</a> on 22 June 1941, initiating nearly four years of <a href="/wiki/Total_war" title="Total war">total war</a>. The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Axis_Powers" title="Axis Powers">Axis</a> initially advanced against desperate but unsuccessful efforts of the <a href="/wiki/Red_Army" title="Red Army">Red Army</a>. In the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Battle_of_Kyiv_(1941)" title="Battle of Kyiv (1941)">battle of Kyiv</a>, the city was acclaimed as a "<a href="/wiki/Hero_City_(Soviet_Union)" title="Hero City (Soviet Union)">Hero City</a>", because of its fierce <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Battle_of_Kyiv_(1941)" title="Battle of Kyiv (1941)">resistance</a>. More than 600,000 Soviet soldiers (or one-quarter of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Soviet_Western_Front" title="Soviet Western Front">Soviet Western Front</a>) were killed or taken captive there, with many suffering <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/German_mistreatment_of_Soviet_prisoners_of_war" title="German mistreatment of Soviet prisoners of war">severe mistreatment</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-102"><a href="#cite_note-102">[97]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-103"><a href="#cite_note-103">[98]</a></sup> After its conquest, most of the Ukrainian SSR was organised within the <a href="/wiki/Reichskommissariat_Ukraine" title="Reichskommissariat Ukraine">Reichskommissariat Ukraine</a>, with the intention of exploiting its resources and eventual German settlement. Some western Ukrainians, who had only joined the Soviet Union in 1939, hailed the Germans as liberators, but that did not last long as the Nazis made little attempt to exploit dissatisfaction with Stalinist policies.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ww2_104-0"><a href="#cite_note-ww2-104">[99]</a></sup> Instead, the Nazis preserved the collective-farm system, carried out <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mass_graves_in_the_Soviet_Union" title="Mass graves in the Soviet Union">genocidal policies</a> against <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_Jews_in_Ukraine" title="History of the Jews in Ukraine">Jews</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/OST-Arbeiter" title="OST-Arbeiter">deported millions of people to work in Germany</a>, and began a depopulation program to prepare for German colonisation.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ww2_104-1"><a href="#cite_note-ww2-104">[99]</a></sup> They blockaded the transport of food on the Dnieper River.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-105"><a href="#cite_note-105">[100]</a></sup>
</p><p>Although the majority of Ukrainians fought in or alongside the Red Army and <a href="/wiki/Soviet_partisans" title="Soviet partisans">Soviet resistance</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-worldwars_106-0"><a href="#cite_note-worldwars-106">[101]</a></sup> in Western Ukraine an independent <a href="/wiki/Ukrainian_Insurgent_Army" title="Ukrainian Insurgent Army">Ukrainian Insurgent Army</a> movement arose (UPA, 1942). It was created as the armed forces of the underground <a href="/wiki/Organization_of_Ukrainian_Nationalists" title="Organization of Ukrainian Nationalists">Organization of Ukrainian Nationalists</a> (OUN).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-107"><a href="#cite_note-107">[102]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-vedeneyev_108-0"><a href="#cite_note-vedeneyev-108">[103]</a></sup> Both organizations, the OUN and the UPA, supported the goal of an <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Declaration_of_Ukrainian_Independence,_1941" title="Declaration of Ukrainian Independence, 1941">independent Ukrainian state</a> on the territory with a Ukrainian ethnic majority. Although this brought conflict with Nazi Germany, at times the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Andriy_Atanasovych_Melnyk" title="Andriy Atanasovych Melnyk">Melnyk</a> wing of the OUN allied with the Nazi forces. From mid-1943 until the end of the war, the UPA carried out <a href="/wiki/Massacres_of_Poles_in_Volhynia_and_Eastern_Galicia" title="Massacres of Poles in Volhynia and Eastern Galicia">massacres of ethnic Poles</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Volhynia" title="Volhynia">Volhynia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Galicia" title="Eastern Galicia">Eastern Galicia</a> regions, killing around 100,000 Polish civilians,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-109"><a href="#cite_note-109">[104]</a></sup> which brought reprisals.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-IPNconf_110-0"><a href="#cite_note-IPNconf-110">[105]</a></sup> These organized massacres were an attempt by the OUN to create a homogeneous Ukrainian state without a Polish minority living within its borders, and to prevent the post-war Polish state from asserting its sovereignty over areas that had been part of pre-war Poland.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-111"><a href="#cite_note-111">[106]</a></sup> After the war, the UPA continued to fight the USSR until the 1950s.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-112"><a href="#cite_note-112">[107]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-113"><a href="#cite_note-113">[108]</a></sup> At the same time, the <a href="/wiki/Ukrainian_Liberation_Army" title="Ukrainian Liberation Army">Ukrainian Liberation Army</a>, another nationalist movement, fought alongside the Nazis.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Kalb2015_114-0"><a href="#cite_note-Kalb2015-114">[109]</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Ruined_Kiev_in_WWII.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1223" data-file-width="1925" decoding="async" height="140" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d6/Ruined_Kiev_in_WWII.jpg/220px-Ruined_Kiev_in_WWII.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d6/Ruined_Kiev_in_WWII.jpg/330px-Ruined_Kiev_in_WWII.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d6/Ruined_Kiev_in_WWII.jpg/440px-Ruined_Kiev_in_WWII.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Ruined_Kiev_in_WWII.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Kyiv" title="Kyiv">Kyiv</a> suffered significant damage during <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Front_(World_War_II)" title="Eastern Front (World War II)">World War II</a>, and was occupied by the <a href="/wiki/Wehrmacht" title="Wehrmacht">Germans</a> from 19 September 1941 until 6 November 1943.</div></div></div>
<p>In total, the number of ethnic Ukrainians who fought in the ranks of the Soviet Army is estimated from 4.5 million<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-worldwars_106-1"><a href="#cite_note-worldwars-106">[101]</a></sup> to 7 million;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-115"><a href="#cite_note-115">[110]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="ref_C1"><a href="#endnote_C1">[c]</a></sup> half of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Soviet_Partisans" title="Soviet Partisans">Pro-Soviet partisan</a> guerrilla resistance units, which counted up to 500,000 troops in 1944, were also Ukrainian.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-116"><a href="#cite_note-116">[111]</a></sup> Generally, the Ukrainian Insurgent Army's figures are unreliable, with figures ranging anywhere from 15,000 to as many as 100,000 fighters.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-117"><a href="#cite_note-117">[112]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-118"><a href="#cite_note-118">[113]</a></sup>
