</p><p>The vast majority of the fighting in World War II took place on the <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Front_(World_War_II)" title="Eastern Front (World War II)">Eastern Front</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-119"><a href="#cite_note-119">[114]</a></sup> By some estimates, 93% of all German casualties took place there.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-120"><a href="#cite_note-120">[115]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/World_War_II_casualties_of_the_Soviet_Union" title="World War II casualties of the Soviet Union">total losses</a> inflicted upon the Ukrainian population during the war are estimated at 6 million,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-121"><a href="#cite_note-121">[116]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-dt-kul-dem-los_122-0"><a href="#cite_note-dt-kul-dem-los-122">[117]</a></sup> including an estimated one and a half million Jews killed by the <a href="/wiki/Einsatzgruppen" title="Einsatzgruppen">Einsatzgruppen</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-123"><a href="#cite_note-123">[118]</a></sup> sometimes with the help of local collaborators. Of the estimated 8.6 million Soviet troop losses,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-peremoga7_124-0"><a href="#cite_note-peremoga7-124">[119]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-125"><a href="#cite_note-125">[120]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Krivosheev_126-0"><a href="#cite_note-Krivosheev-126">[121]</a></sup> 1.4 million were ethnic <a href="/wiki/Ukrainians" title="Ukrainians">Ukrainians</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-peremoga7_124-1"><a href="#cite_note-peremoga7-124">[119]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Krivosheev_126-1"><a href="#cite_note-Krivosheev-126">[121]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="ref_C2"><a href="#endnote_C2">[c]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="ref_Dnone"><a href="#endnote_Dnone">[d]</a></sup> and general losses of the Ukrainian people in the war amounted to 40–44% of the total losses of the USSR.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-127"><a href="#cite_note-127">[122]</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template noprint noexcerpt Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Wikipedia:NOTRS" title="Wikipedia:NOTRS"><span title="Unreliable? (August 2022)">better source needed</span></a></i>]</sup> The <a href="/wiki/Victory_Day_over_Nazism_in_World_War_II" title="Victory Day over Nazism in World War II">Victory Day</a> is celebrated as one of eleven Ukrainian national holidays.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-128"><a href="#cite_note-128">[123]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span id="Post.E2.80.93war_Soviet_Ukraine"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Post–war_Soviet_Ukraine">Post–war Soviet Ukraine</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Ukrainian_Soviet_Socialist_Republic" title="Ukrainian Soviet Socialist Republic">Ukrainian Soviet Socialist Republic</a>, <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_Soviet_Union_(1953%E2%80%931964)" title="History of the Soviet Union (1953–1964)">History of the Soviet Union (1953–1964)</a>, <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_Soviet_Union_(1964%E2%80%931982)" title="History of the Soviet Union (1964–1982)">History of the Soviet Union (1964–1982)</a>, and <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_Soviet_Union_(1982%E2%80%931991)" title="History of the Soviet Union (1982–1991)">History of the Soviet Union (1982–1991)</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Khrushchev_and_Brezhnev.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="750" data-file-width="432" decoding="async" height="295" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/c/c8/Khrushchev_and_Brezhnev.jpg/170px-Khrushchev_and_Brezhnev.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/c/c8/Khrushchev_and_Brezhnev.jpg/255px-Khrushchev_and_Brezhnev.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/c/c8/Khrushchev_and_Brezhnev.jpg/340px-Khrushchev_and_Brezhnev.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Khrushchev_and_Brezhnev.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Two future leaders of the <a href="/wiki/Soviet_Union" title="Soviet Union">Soviet Union</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nikita_Khrushchev" title="Nikita Khrushchev">Nikita Khrushchev</a> (left, pre-war <a href="/wiki/Communist_Party_of_the_Soviet_Union" title="Communist Party of the Soviet Union">CPSU</a> chief in Ukraine) and <a href="/wiki/Leonid_Brezhnev" title="Leonid Brezhnev">Leonid Brezhnev</a> (an engineer from <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kamianske" title="Kamianske">Kamianske</a>)</div></div></div>
<p>The republic was heavily damaged by the war, and it required significant efforts to recover. More than 700 cities and towns and 28,000 villages were destroyed.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-129"><a href="#cite_note-129">[124]</a></sup> The situation was worsened by a <a href="/wiki/Famine" title="Famine">famine</a> in 1946–1947, which was caused by a drought and the wartime destruction of infrastructure, killing at least tens of thousands of people.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-dt-kul-dem-los_122-1"><a href="#cite_note-dt-kul-dem-los-122">[117]</a></sup> In 1945, the Ukrainian SSR became one of the founding members of the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">United Nations</a> (UN),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-un_ukssr_130-0"><a href="#cite_note-un_ukssr-130">[125]</a></sup> part of a special agreement at the <a href="/wiki/Yalta_Conference" title="Yalta Conference">Yalta Conference</a>, and, alongside Belarus, had voting rights in the UN even though they were not independent.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-131"><a href="#cite_note-131">[126]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-132"><a href="#cite_note-132">[127]</a></sup> Moreover, Ukraine once more expanded its borders as it annexed <a href="/wiki/Zakarpattia_Oblast" title="Zakarpattia Oblast">Zakarpattia</a>, and the population became much more homogenized due to post-war <a href="/wiki/Population_transfer_in_the_Soviet_Union" title="Population transfer in the Soviet Union">population transfers</a>, most of which, as in the case of <a href="/wiki/Flight_and_expulsion_of_Germans_(1944%E2%80%931950)" title="Flight and expulsion of Germans (1944–1950)">Germans</a> and <a href="/wiki/Deportation_of_the_Crimean_Tatars" title="Deportation of the Crimean Tatars">Crimean Tatars</a>, were forced. As of 1 January 1953, Ukrainians were second only to Russians among adult "<a href="/wiki/Forced_settlements_in_the_Soviet_Union" title="Forced settlements in the Soviet Union">special deportees</a>", comprising 20% of the total.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Malynovska_133-0"><a href="#cite_note-Malynovska-133">[128]</a></sup>
</p><p>Following the death of Stalin in 1953, <a href="/wiki/Nikita_Khrushchev" title="Nikita Khrushchev">Nikita Khrushchev</a> became the new leader of the USSR, who began the policies of <a href="/wiki/De-Stalinization" title="De-Stalinization">De-Stalinization</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Khrushchev_Thaw" title="Khrushchev Thaw">Khrushchev Thaw</a>. During his term as head of the Soviet Union, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Crimean_Oblast" title="Crimean Oblast">Crimea</a> was <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/1954_transfer_of_Crimea" title="1954 transfer of Crimea">transferred</a> from the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Russian_SFSR" title="Russian SFSR">Russian SFSR</a> to the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ukrainian_SSR" title="Ukrainian SSR">Ukrainian SSR</a>, formally as a friendship gift to Ukraine and for economic reasons.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-134"><a href="#cite_note-134">[129]</a></sup> This represented the final extension of Ukrainian territory and formed the basis for the internationally recognized borders of Ukraine to this day. Ukraine was one of the most important republics of the Soviet Union, which resulted in many top positions in the Soviet Union occupied by Ukrainians, including notably <a href="/wiki/Leonid_Brezhnev" title="Leonid Brezhnev">Leonid Brezhnev</a>, <a href="/wiki/General_Secretary_of_the_Communist_Party_of_the_Soviet_Union" title="General Secretary of the Communist Party of the Soviet Union">General Secretary of the Communist Party of the Soviet Union</a> from 1964 to 1982. However, it was him and his <a href="/wiki/Communist_Party_of_Ukraine_(Soviet_Union)" title="Communist Party of Ukraine (Soviet Union)">appointee in Ukraine</a>, <a href="/wiki/Volodymyr_Shcherbytsky" title="Volodymyr Shcherbytsky">Volodymyr Shcherbytsky</a>, who presided over extensive <a href="/wiki/Russification_of_Ukraine" title="Russification of Ukraine">Russification</a> of Ukraine and who were instrumental in repressing a new generation of Ukrainian intellectuals known as the <a href="/wiki/Sixtiers" title="Sixtiers">Sixtiers</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-135"><a href="#cite_note-135">[130]</a></sup>
</p><p>By 1950, the republic had fully surpassed pre-war levels of industry and production.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-136"><a href="#cite_note-136">[131]</a></sup> Soviet Ukraine soon became a European leader in industrial production<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-137"><a href="#cite_note-137">[132]</a></sup> and an important centre of the Soviet <a href="/wiki/Arms_industry" title="Arms industry">arms industry</a> and high-tech research, though heavy industry still had an outsided influence.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-138"><a href="#cite_note-138">[133]</a></sup> The Soviet government invested in hydroelectric and nuclear power projects to cater to the energy demand that the development carried. On 26 April 1986, however, a reactor in the <a href="/wiki/Chernobyl_Nuclear_Power_Plant" title="Chernobyl Nuclear Power Plant">Chernobyl Nuclear Power Plant</a> exploded, resulting in the <a href="/wiki/Chernobyl_disaster" title="Chernobyl disaster">Chernobyl disaster</a>, the worst <a href="/wiki/Nuclear_reactor" title="Nuclear reactor">nuclear reactor</a> accident in history.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-139"><a href="#cite_note-139">[134]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Independence">Independence</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Dissolution_of_the_Soviet_Union" title="Dissolution of the Soviet Union">Dissolution of the Soviet Union</a>, <a href="/wiki/Modern_history_of_Ukraine" title="Modern history of Ukraine">Modern history of Ukraine</a>, <a href="/wiki/Orange_Revolution" title="Orange Revolution">Orange Revolution</a>, <a href="/wiki/Euromaidan" title="Euromaidan">Euromaidan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Revolution_of_Dignity" title="Revolution of Dignity">Revolution of Dignity</a>, <a href="/wiki/Russo-Ukrainian_War" title="Russo-Ukrainian War">Russo-Ukrainian War</a>, and <a href="/wiki/2022_Russian_invasion_of_Ukraine" title="2022 Russian invasion of Ukraine">2022 Russian invasion of Ukraine</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:RIAN_archive_848095_Signing_the_Agreement_to_eliminate_the_USSR_and_establish_the_Commonwealth_of_Independent_States.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1000" data-file-width="1500" decoding="async" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/43/RIAN_archive_848095_Signing_the_Agreement_to_eliminate_the_USSR_and_establish_the_Commonwealth_of_Independent_States.jpg/220px-RIAN_archive_848095_Signing_the_Agreement_to_eliminate_the_USSR_and_establish_the_Commonwealth_of_Independent_States.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/43/RIAN_archive_848095_Signing_the_Agreement_to_eliminate_the_USSR_and_establish_the_Commonwealth_of_Independent_States.jpg/330px-RIAN_archive_848095_Signing_the_Agreement_to_eliminate_the_USSR_and_establish_the_Commonwealth_of_Independent_States.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/43/RIAN_archive_848095_Signing_the_Agreement_to_eliminate_the_USSR_and_establish_the_Commonwealth_of_Independent_States.jpg/440px-RIAN_archive_848095_Signing_the_Agreement_to_eliminate_the_USSR_and_establish_the_Commonwealth_of_Independent_States.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:RIAN_archive_848095_Signing_the_Agreement_to_eliminate_the_USSR_and_establish_the_Commonwealth_of_Independent_States.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Ukrainian President <a href="/wiki/Leonid_Kravchuk" title="Leonid Kravchuk">Leonid Kravchuk</a> and Russian President <a href="/wiki/Boris_Yeltsin" title="Boris Yeltsin">Boris Yeltsin</a> signing the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Belavezha_Accords" title="Belavezha Accords">Belavezha Accords</a>, which <a href="/wiki/Dissolution_of_the_Soviet_Union" title="Dissolution of the Soviet Union">dissolved the Soviet Union</a>, on 8 December 1991</div></div></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Mikhail_Gorbachev" title="Mikhail Gorbachev">Mikhail Gorbachev</a> pursued a policy of limited liberalization of public life, known as <i><a href="/wiki/Perestroika" title="Perestroika">perestroika</a>,</i> and attempted to reform a <a href="/wiki/Era_of_Stagnation" title="Era of Stagnation">stagnating economy</a>. The latter failed, but the democratization of the Soviet Union fuelled nationalist and separatist tendencies among the ethnic minorities, including Ukrainians.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-140"><a href="#cite_note-140">[135]</a></sup> As part of the so-called <a href="/wiki/Parade_of_sovereignties" title="Parade of sovereignties">parade of sovereignties</a>, on 16 July 1990, the newly elected <a href="/wiki/Supreme_Soviet_of_the_Ukrainian_Soviet_Socialist_Republic" title="Supreme Soviet of the Ukrainian Soviet Socialist Republic">Supreme Soviet of the Ukrainian Soviet Socialist Republic</a> adopted the <a href="/wiki/Declaration_of_State_Sovereignty_of_Ukraine" title="Declaration of State Sovereignty of Ukraine">Declaration of State Sovereignty of Ukraine</a>;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-141"><a href="#cite_note-141">[136]</a></sup> after a <a href="/wiki/1991_Soviet_coup_d%27%C3%A9tat_attempt" title="1991 Soviet coup d'état attempt">putsch</a> of some Communist leaders in Moscow failed to depose Gorbachov, outright independence was <a href="/wiki/Declaration_of_Independence_of_Ukraine" title="Declaration of Independence of Ukraine">proclaimed</a> on 24 August 1991<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-142"><a href="#cite_note-142">[137]</a></sup> and approved by 92% of the Ukrainian electorate in a <a href="/wiki/1991_Ukrainian_independence_referendum" title="1991 Ukrainian independence referendum">referendum</a> on 1 December.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Nohlen_Stöver_143-0"><a href="#cite_note-Nohlen_Stöver-143">[138]</a></sup> Ukraine's new <a href="/wiki/President_of_Ukraine" title="President of Ukraine">President</a>, Leonid Kravchuk, went on to sign the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Belavezha_Accords" title="Belavezha Accords">Belavezha Accords</a> and made Ukraine a founding member of the much looser <a href="/wiki/Commonwealth_of_Independent_States" title="Commonwealth of Independent States">Commonwealth of Independent States</a> (CIS),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-144"><a href="#cite_note-144">[139]</a></sup> though Ukraine never became a full member of the latter as it did not ratify the agreement founding CIS.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:2_145-0"><a href="#cite_note-:2-145">[140]</a></sup> These documents sealed the fate of the Soviet Union, which formally voted itself out of existence on 26 December.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-146"><a href="#cite_note-146">[141]</a></sup>
</p><p>Ukraine was initially viewed as having favourable economic conditions in comparison to the other regions of the Soviet Union,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-147"><a href="#cite_note-147">[142]</a></sup> though it was one of the poorer Soviet republics by the end of the Soviet Union.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Notstronk_148-0"><a href="#cite_note-Notstronk-148">[143]</a></sup> However, during its transition to the market economy, the country experienced deeper economic slowdown than almost all of the other <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Former_Soviet_Republics" title="Former Soviet Republics">former Soviet Republics</a>. During the recession, between 1991 and 1999, Ukraine lost 60% of its GDP<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-IMF_149-0"><a href="#cite_note-IMF-149">[144]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-150"><a href="#cite_note-150">[145]</a></sup> and suffered from <a href="/wiki/Hyperinflation" title="Hyperinflation">hyperinflation</a> that peaked at 10,000% in 1993.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-151"><a href="#cite_note-151">[146]</a></sup> The situation only stabilized well after the new currency, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hryvnia" title="Hryvnia">hryvnia</a>, fell sharply in late 1998 partially as a fallout from the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Russian_debt_default" title="Russian debt default">Russian debt default</a> earlier that year.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-152"><a href="#cite_note-152">[147]</a></sup> The legacy of the economic policies of the nineties was the mass privatization of state property that created a class of extremely powerful and rich individuals known as the <a href="/wiki/Ukrainian_oligarch" title="Ukrainian oligarch">oligarchs</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Notstronk_148-1"><a href="#cite_note-Notstronk-148">[143]</a></sup> The country would then fall into sharp recessions as a result of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/2008_global_financial_crisis" title="2008 global financial crisis">2008 global financial crisis</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Notstronk_148-2"><a href="#cite_note-Notstronk-148">[143]</a></sup> then the start of the <a href="/wiki/Russo-Ukrainian_War" title="Russo-Ukrainian War">Russo-Ukrainian War</a> in 2014,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-153"><a href="#cite_note-153">[148]</a></sup> and finally, the <a href="/wiki/2022_Russian_invasion_of_Ukraine" title="2022 Russian invasion of Ukraine">full-scale invasion</a> of Russia in starting from 24 February 2022.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-154"><a href="#cite_note-154">[149]</a></sup> Ukraine's economy in general underperformed since the time independence came due to pervasive <a href="/wiki/Corruption_in_Ukraine" title="Corruption in Ukraine">corruption</a> and mismanagement,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-155"><a href="#cite_note-155">[150]</a></sup> which, particularly in the 1990s, led to protests and organized strikes.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-156"><a href="#cite_note-156">[151]</a></sup> The war with Russia impeded meaningful economic recovery in the 2010s,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-157"><a href="#cite_note-157">[152]</a></sup> while efforts to combat the <a href="/wiki/COVID-19_pandemic_in_Ukraine" title="COVID-19 pandemic in Ukraine">COVID-19 pandemic</a>, which arrived in 2020, were made much harder by <a href="/wiki/COVID-19_vaccine" title="COVID-19 vaccine">low vaccination rates</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-158"><a href="#cite_note-158">[153]</a></sup> and, later in the pandemic, by the ongoing invasion.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-159"><a href="#cite_note-159">[154]</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Morning_first_day_of_Orange_Revolution.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1712" data-file-width="2288" decoding="async" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f8/Morning_first_day_of_Orange_Revolution.jpg/220px-Morning_first_day_of_Orange_Revolution.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f8/Morning_first_day_of_Orange_Revolution.jpg/330px-Morning_first_day_of_Orange_Revolution.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f8/Morning_first_day_of_Orange_Revolution.jpg/440px-Morning_first_day_of_Orange_Revolution.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Morning_first_day_of_Orange_Revolution.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Protesters at <a href="/wiki/Maidan_Nezalezhnosti" title="Maidan Nezalezhnosti">Independence Square</a> on the first day of the <a href="/wiki/Orange_Revolution" title="Orange Revolution">Orange Revolution</a></div></div></div><p> From the political perspective, one of the defining features of the <a href="/wiki/Politics_of_Ukraine" title="Politics of Ukraine">politics of Ukraine</a> is that for most of the time, it has been divided along two issues: the relation between Ukraine, the <a href="/wiki/Western_world" title="Western world">West</a> and Russia, and the classical <a href="/wiki/Left%E2%80%93right_political_spectrum" title="Left–right political spectrum">left-right</a> divide.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-160"><a href="#cite_note-160">[155]</a></sup> The first two presidents, Kravchuk and <a href="/wiki/Leonid_Kuchma" title="Leonid Kuchma">Leonid Kuchma</a>, tended to balance the competing visions of Ukraine,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-161"><a href="#cite_note-161">[156]</a></sup> though <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Yushchenko" title="Yushchenko">Yushchenko</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Yanukovych" title="Yanukovych">Yanukovych</a> were generally pro-Western and pro-Russian, respectively. There were two major protests against Yanukovych: the <a href="/wiki/Orange_Revolution" title="Orange Revolution">Orange Revolution</a> in 2004, when tens of thousands of people went in protest of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Election_rigging" title="Election rigging">election rigging</a> in his favour (Yushchenko was eventually elected president), and another one in the winter of 2013/2014, when more gathered on the <a href="/wiki/Euromaidan" title="Euromaidan">Euromaidan</a> to oppose the Yanukovych's refusal to sign the <a href="/wiki/European_Union%E2%80%93Ukraine_Association_Agreement" title="European Union–Ukraine Association Agreement">European Union–Ukraine Association Agreement</a>. By the end of the 2014 protests, he fled from Ukraine and was removed by the parliament in what is termed the <a href="/wiki/Revolution_of_Dignity" title="Revolution of Dignity">Revolution of Dignity</a>, but Russia refused to recognize the interim pro-Western government, calling it a <i><a href="/wiki/Military_junta" title="Military junta">junta</a></i> and denouncing the events as a <a href="/wiki/Coup_d%27%C3%A9tat" title="Coup d'état">coup d'état</a> sponsored by the United States.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-162"><a href="#cite_note-162">[157]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-163"><a href="#cite_note-163">[158]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Partido_da_imprensa_Golpista_164-0"><a href="#cite_note-Partido_da_imprensa_Golpista-164">[159]</a></sup>
</p><p>Even though Russia had signed the so-called <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Budapest_Memorandum_on_Security_Assurances" title="Budapest Memorandum on Security Assurances">Budapest memorandum</a> in 1994 that said that Ukraine was to hand over <a href="/wiki/Ukraine_and_weapons_of_mass_destruction" title="Ukraine and weapons of mass destruction">nuclear weapons</a> in exchange of security guarantees and those of territorial integrity, it reacted violently to these developments and started a <a href="/wiki/Russo-Ukrainian_War" title="Russo-Ukrainian War">war against its western neighbour</a>. In late February and early March 2014, it <a href="/wiki/Annexation_of_Crimea_by_the_Russian_Federation" title="Annexation of Crimea by the Russian Federation">annexed Crimea</a> using its <a href="/wiki/Russian_Navy" title="Russian Navy">Navy</a> in <a href="/wiki/Sevastopol_Naval_Base" title="Sevastopol Naval Base">Sevastopol</a> as well as the so-called <a href="/wiki/Little_green_men_(Russo-Ukrainian_War)" title="Little green men (Russo-Ukrainian War)">little green men</a>; after this succeeded, it then launched a <a href="/wiki/War_in_Donbas_(2014%E2%80%932022)" title="War in Donbas (2014–2022)">proxy war in the Donbas</a> via the breakaway <a href="/wiki/Donetsk_People%27s_Republic" title="Donetsk People's Republic">Donetsk People's Republic</a> and <a href="/wiki/Luhansk_People%27s_Republic" title="Luhansk People's Republic">Luhansk People's Republic</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-165"><a href="#cite_note-165">[160]</a></sup> The first months of the conflict with the Russian-backed separatists were fluid, but Russian forces then started an open invasion in Donbas on 24 August 2014. Together they pushed back Ukrainian troops to the frontline established in February 2015, i.e. after Ukrainian troops <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Debaltseve" title="Battle of Debaltseve">withdrew from Debaltseve</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-166"><a href="#cite_note-166">[161]</a></sup> The conflict remained in a sort of a <a href="/wiki/Frozen_conflict" title="Frozen conflict">frozen state</a> until the early hours of 24 February 2022,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-167"><a href="#cite_note-167">[162]</a></sup> when Russia proceeded with an <a href="/wiki/2022_Russian_invasion_of_Ukraine" title="2022 Russian invasion of Ukraine">ongoing invasion</a> of Ukraine (euphemized in Russia as a "special military operation").<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-168"><a href="#cite_note-168">[163]</a></sup> Russian troops now control about 20% of Ukraine's internationally recognized territory,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-169"><a href="#cite_note-169">[164]</a></sup> though Russia was not able to realize its stated objective of taking full control of the country.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-170"><a href="#cite_note-170">[165]</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:2022_Russian_invasion_of_Ukraine.svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1478" data-file-width="2199" decoding="async" height="148" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4f/2022_Russian_invasion_of_Ukraine.svg/220px-2022_Russian_invasion_of_Ukraine.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4f/2022_Russian_invasion_of_Ukraine.svg/330px-2022_Russian_invasion_of_Ukraine.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4f/2022_Russian_invasion_of_Ukraine.svg/440px-2022_Russian_invasion_of_Ukraine.svg.png 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:2022_Russian_invasion_of_Ukraine.svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Current control of Ukraine by Russian troops</div></div></div>
<p>The military conflict with Russia shifted the government's policy towards the West. Shortly after Yanukovych fled Ukraine, the country signed the EU association agreement in June 2014, and its citizens were granted visa-free travel to the European Union three years later. In January 2019, the <a href="/wiki/Orthodox_Church_of_Ukraine" title="Orthodox Church of Ukraine">Orthodox Church of Ukraine</a> was recognized as independent of Moscow, which reversed the <a href="/wiki/Annexation_of_the_Metropolitanate_of_Kyiv_by_the_Moscow_Patriarchate" title="Annexation of the Metropolitanate of Kyiv by the Moscow Patriarchate">1686 decision</a> of the patriarch of Constantinople and dealt a further blow to Moscow's influence in Ukraine.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-171"><a href="#cite_note-171">[166]</a></sup> Finally, amid a full-scale war with Russia, Ukraine was granted <a href="/wiki/Potential_enlargement_of_the_European_Union" title="Potential enlargement of the European Union">candidate status</a> to the European Union on 23 June 2022.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BBC_News_172-0"><a href="#cite_note-BBC_News-172">[167]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Geography">Geography</span></h2>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Geography_of_Ukraine" title="Geography of Ukraine">Geography of Ukraine</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Topographic_map_of_Ukraine_(with_borders_and_towns).svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="959" data-file-width="1449" decoding="async" height="146" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ac/Topographic_map_of_Ukraine_%28with_borders_and_towns%29.svg/220px-Topographic_map_of_Ukraine_%28with_borders_and_towns%29.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ac/Topographic_map_of_Ukraine_%28with_borders_and_towns%29.svg/330px-Topographic_map_of_Ukraine_%28with_borders_and_towns%29.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ac/Topographic_map_of_Ukraine_%28with_borders_and_towns%29.svg/440px-Topographic_map_of_Ukraine_%28with_borders_and_towns%29.svg.png 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Topographic_map_of_Ukraine_(with_borders_and_towns).svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Topographic map of Ukraine (with borders and towns)</div></div></div>
<p>Ukraine is the <a href="/wiki/List_of_European_countries_by_area" title="List of European countries by area">second-largest European country</a>, after Russia. Lying between latitudes <a href="/wiki/44th_parallel_north" title="44th parallel north">44°</a> and <a href="/wiki/53rd_parallel_north" title="53rd parallel north">53° N</a>, and longitudes <a href="/wiki/22nd_meridian_east" title="22nd meridian east">22°</a> and <a href="/wiki/41st_meridian_east" title="41st meridian east">41° E</a>., it is mostly in the <a href="/wiki/East_European_Plain" title="East European Plain">East European Plain</a>. Ukraine covers an area of 603,628 square kilometres (233,062 sq mi), with a coastline of 2,782 kilometres (1,729 mi).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cia_55-1"><a href="#cite_note-cia-55">[50]</a></sup>
</p><p>The landscape of Ukraine consists mostly of fertile <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Steppes" title="Steppes">steppes</a> (plains with few trees) and plateaus, crossed by rivers such as the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dnieper_River" title="Dnieper River">Dnieper</a> (<span title="Ukrainian-language text"><i lang="uk-Latn">Dnipro</i></span>), <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Seversky_Donets" title="Seversky Donets">Seversky Donets</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dniester" title="Dniester">Dniester</a> and the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Southern_Bug" title="Southern Bug">Southern Bug</a> as they flow south into the <a href="/wiki/Black_Sea" title="Black Sea">Black Sea</a> and the smaller <a href="/wiki/Sea_of_Azov" title="Sea of Azov">Sea of Azov</a>. To the southwest, the <a href="/wiki/Danube_Delta" title="Danube Delta">delta</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Danube" title="Danube">Danube</a> forms the border with Romania. Ukraine's various regions have diverse geographic features ranging from the highlands to the lowlands. The country's only mountains are the <a href="/wiki/Carpathian_Mountains" title="Carpathian Mountains">Carpathian Mountains</a> in the west, of which the highest is <a href="/wiki/Hoverla" title="Hoverla">Hoverla</a> at 2,061 metres (6,762 ft), and the <a href="/wiki/Crimean_Mountains" title="Crimean Mountains">Crimean Mountains</a>, in the extreme south along the coast.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-173"><a href="#cite_note-173">[168]</a></sup>
</p><p>Ukraine also has a number of highland regions such as the <a href="/wiki/Volhynian-Podolian_Upland" title="Volhynian-Podolian Upland">Volyn-Podillia Upland</a> (in the west) and the Near-Dnipro Upland (on the right bank of the Dnieper). To the east there are the south-western spurs of the <a href="/wiki/Central_Russian_Upland" title="Central Russian Upland">Central Russian Upland</a> over which runs the border with Russia. Near the <a href="/wiki/Sea_of_Azov" title="Sea of Azov">Sea of Azov</a> are the Donets Ridge and the Near Azov Upland. The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Snow_melt" title="Snow melt">snow melt</a> from the mountains feeds the rivers and their <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Waterfalls_of_Ukraine" title="Waterfalls of Ukraine">waterfalls</a>.
</p><p>Significant natural resources in Ukraine include <a href="/wiki/Lithium" title="Lithium">lithium</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-174"><a href="#cite_note-174">[169]</a></sup> natural gas,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:0_175-0"><a href="#cite_note-:0-175">[170]</a></sup> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kaolin" title="Kaolin">kaolin</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:0_175-1"><a href="#cite_note-:0-175">[170]</a></sup> timber<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-176"><a href="#cite_note-176">[171]</a></sup> and an abundance of <a href="/wiki/Arable_land" title="Arable land">arable land</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-177"><a href="#cite_note-177">[172]</a></sup> Ukraine has many environmental issues.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-178"><a href="#cite_note-178">[173]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-179"><a href="#cite_note-179">[174]</a></sup> Some regions lack adequate supplies of potable water.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-180"><a href="#cite_note-180">[175]</a></sup> Air and water pollution affects the country, as well as deforestation, and radiation contamination in the northeast from the 1986 accident at the <a href="/wiki/Chernobyl" title="Chernobyl">Chernobyl</a> Nuclear Power Plant.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-181"><a href="#cite_note-181">[176]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Climate">Climate</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:262px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Koppen-Geiger_Map_UKR_present.svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="850" data-file-width="1816" decoding="async" height="122" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Koppen-Geiger_Map_UKR_present.svg/260px-Koppen-Geiger_Map_UKR_present.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Koppen-Geiger_Map_UKR_present.svg/390px-Koppen-Geiger_Map_UKR_present.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Koppen-Geiger_Map_UKR_present.svg/520px-Koppen-Geiger_Map_UKR_present.svg.png 2x" width="260"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Koppen-Geiger_Map_UKR_present.svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification" title="Köppen climate classification">Köppen climate classification</a> map of Ukraine</div></div></div>
<p>Ukraine has a mostly <a href="/wiki/Temperate_climate" title="Temperate climate">temperate climate</a>, except for the southern coast of Crimea which has a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Subtropical_climate" title="Subtropical climate">subtropical climate</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-faoclimate_182-0"><a href="#cite_note-faoclimate-182">[177]</a></sup> The climate is influenced by moderately warm, humid air from the Atlantic Ocean.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ebclimate_183-0"><a href="#cite_note-ebclimate-183">[178]</a></sup> Average annual temperatures range from 5.5–7 °C (41.9–44.6 °F) in the north, to 11–13 °C (51.8–55.4 °F) in the south.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ebclimate_183-1"><a href="#cite_note-ebclimate-183">[178]</a></sup> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Precipitation_(meteorology)" title="Precipitation (meteorology)">Precipitation</a> is highest in the west and north and lowest in the east and southeast.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ebclimate_183-2"><a href="#cite_note-ebclimate-183">[178]</a></sup> Western Ukraine, particularly in the Carpathian Mountains, receives around 120 centimetres (47.2 in) of precipitation annually, while Crimea and the coastal areas of the Black Sea receive around 40 centimetres (15.7 in).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ebclimate_183-3"><a href="#cite_note-ebclimate-183">[178]</a></sup>
</p><p>Water availability from the major river basins is expected to decrease <a href="/wiki/Effects_of_climate_change" title="Effects of climate change">due to climate change</a>, especially in summer. This poses risks to the agricultural sector.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-184"><a href="#cite_note-184">[179]</a></sup> The negative <a href="/wiki/Effects_of_climate_change_on_agriculture" title="Effects of climate change on agriculture">impacts of climate change on agriculture</a> are mostly felt in the south of the country, which has a <a href="/wiki/Steppe" title="Steppe">steppe</a> climate. In the north, some crops may be able to benefit from a longer growing season.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-185"><a href="#cite_note-185">[180]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/World_Bank" title="World Bank">World Bank</a> has stated that Ukraine is highly <a href="/wiki/Climate_change_vulnerability" title="Climate change vulnerability">vulnerable to climate change</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-186"><a href="#cite_note-186">[181]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Biodiversity">Biodiversity</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Wildlife_of_Ukraine" title="Wildlife of Ukraine">Wildlife of Ukraine</a></div>
<p>Ukraine contains six terrestrial <a href="/wiki/Ecoregion" title="Ecoregion">ecoregions</a>: <a href="/wiki/Central_European_mixed_forests" title="Central European mixed forests">Central European mixed forests</a>, <a href="/wiki/Crimean_Submediterranean_forest_complex" title="Crimean Submediterranean forest complex">Crimean Submediterranean forest complex</a>, <a href="/wiki/East_European_forest_steppe" title="East European forest steppe">East European forest steppe</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pannonian_mixed_forests" title="Pannonian mixed forests">Pannonian mixed forests</a>, <a href="/wiki/Carpathian_montane_conifer_forests" title="Carpathian montane conifer forests">Carpathian montane conifer forests</a>, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pontic_steppe" title="Pontic steppe">Pontic steppe</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-DinersteinOlson2017_187-0"><a href="#cite_note-DinersteinOlson2017-187">[182]</a></sup> There is somewhat more <a href="/wiki/Conifer" title="Conifer">coniferous</a> than <a href="/wiki/Deciduous" title="Deciduous">deciduous</a> forest.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ShvidenkoBukshaKrakovska2017_188-0"><a href="#cite_note-ShvidenkoBukshaKrakovska2017-188">[183]</a></sup> The most densely forested area is <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Polisia" title="Polisia">Polisia</a> in the northwest, with pine, oak, and birch.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ShvidenkoBukshaKrakovska2017_188-1"><a href="#cite_note-ShvidenkoBukshaKrakovska2017-188">[183]</a></sup> There are 45,000 species of animal,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Conference2001_189-0"><a href="#cite_note-Conference2001-189">[184]</a></sup> with approximately 385 endangered species listed in the <a href="/wiki/Red_Data_Book_of_Ukraine" title="Red Data Book of Ukraine">Red Data Book of Ukraine</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-State_190-0"><a href="#cite_note-State-190">[185]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Ramsar_site" title="Ramsar site">Internationally important wetlands</a> cover over 7,000 square kilometres (2,700 sq mi), with the <a href="/wiki/Danube_Delta" title="Danube Delta">Danube Delta</a> being important for conservation.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-wetland_191-0"><a href="#cite_note-wetland-191">[186]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ramsar_192-0"><a href="#cite_note-Ramsar-192">[187]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Urban_areas">Urban areas</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/List_of_cities_in_Ukraine" title="List of cities in Ukraine">List of cities in Ukraine</a></div>
<p>Ukraine has 457 cities, of which 176 are designated as oblast-class, 279 as smaller <span title="Ukrainian-language text"><i lang="uk-Latn">raion</i></span>-class cities, and two as special legal status cities. There are also 886 urban-type settlements and 28,552 villages.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-oblasts_193-0"><a href="#cite_note-oblasts-193">[188]</a></sup>
</p>
