<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Politics">Politics</span></h2>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Politics_of_Ukraine" title="Politics of Ukraine">Politics of Ukraine</a>, <a href="/wiki/Government_of_Ukraine" title="Government of Ukraine">Government of Ukraine</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Elections_in_Ukraine" title="Elections in Ukraine">Elections in Ukraine</a></div>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Russo-Ukrainian_War" title="Russo-Ukrainian War">Russo-Ukrainian War</a> and <a href="/wiki/2022_Russian_invasion_of_Ukraine" title="2022 Russian invasion of Ukraine">2022 Russian invasion of Ukraine</a></div>
<p>Ukraine is a republic under a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Semi-presidential_system" title="Semi-presidential system">semi-presidential system</a> with separate <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Legislative_branch" title="Legislative branch">legislative</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Executive_branch" title="Executive branch">executive</a>, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Judicial_branch" title="Judicial branch">judicial branches</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Choudhry_2018_p16._194-0"><a href="#cite_note-Choudhry_2018_p16.-194">[189]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Constitution">Constitution</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_Ukraine" title="Constitution of Ukraine">Constitution of Ukraine</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:262px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Chart_Constitution_of_Ukraine_EN.svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="744" data-file-width="1052" decoding="async" height="184" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3d/Chart_Constitution_of_Ukraine_EN.svg/260px-Chart_Constitution_of_Ukraine_EN.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3d/Chart_Constitution_of_Ukraine_EN.svg/390px-Chart_Constitution_of_Ukraine_EN.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3d/Chart_Constitution_of_Ukraine_EN.svg/520px-Chart_Constitution_of_Ukraine_EN.svg.png 2x" width="260"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Chart_Constitution_of_Ukraine_EN.svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Chart of the political system of Ukraine</div></div></div>
<p>The Constitution of Ukraine was adopted and ratified at the 5th session of the <a href="/wiki/Verkhovna_Rada" title="Verkhovna Rada">Verkhovna Rada</a>, the parliament of Ukraine, on 28 June 1996.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-UNIANCD28616_195-0"><a href="#cite_note-UNIANCD28616-195">[190]</a></sup> The constitution was passed with 315 ayes out of 450 votes possible (300 ayes minimum).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-UNIANCD28616_195-1"><a href="#cite_note-UNIANCD28616-195">[190]</a></sup> All other laws and other normative<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="margin-left:0.1em; white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Please_clarify" title="Wikipedia:Please clarify"><span title="The text near this tag may need clarification or removal of jargon. (March 2022)">clarification needed</span></a></i>]</sup> legal acts of Ukraine must conform to the constitution. The right to amend the constitution through a special legislative procedure is vested exclusively in the parliament. The only body that may interpret the constitution and determine whether legislation conforms to it is the <a href="/wiki/Constitutional_Court_of_Ukraine" title="Constitutional Court of Ukraine">Constitutional Court of Ukraine</a>. Since 1996, the <a href="/wiki/Public_holiday" title="Public holiday">public holiday</a> <a href="/wiki/Constitution_Day_(Ukraine)" title="Constitution Day (Ukraine)">Constitution Day</a> is celebrated on 28 June.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-196"><a href="#cite_note-196">[191]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-UW29121996_197-0"><a href="#cite_note-UW29121996-197">[192]</a></sup> On 7 February 2019, the Verkhovna Rada voted to amend the constitution to state Ukraine's strategic objectives as joining the <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a> and <a href="/wiki/NATO" title="NATO">NATO</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-198"><a href="#cite_note-198">[193]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span id="President.2C_parliament_and_government"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="President,_parliament_and_government">President, parliament and government</span></h3>
<table class="wikitable floatright" style="text-align:center;">
<tbody><tr>
<td><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Volodymyr_Zelensky_Official_portrait.jpg"><img alt="Volodymyr Zelensky Official portrait.jpg" data-file-height="4724" data-file-width="3488" decoding="async" height="191" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9c/Volodymyr_Zelensky_Official_portrait.jpg/141px-Volodymyr_Zelensky_Official_portrait.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9c/Volodymyr_Zelensky_Official_portrait.jpg/212px-Volodymyr_Zelensky_Official_portrait.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9c/Volodymyr_Zelensky_Official_portrait.jpg/282px-Volodymyr_Zelensky_Official_portrait.jpg 2x" width="141"/></a>
</td>
<td><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:%D0%94%D0%B5%D0%BD%D0%B8%D1%81_%D0%A8%D0%BC%D1%8B%D0%B3%D0%B0%D0%BB%D1%8C_(%D0%BF%D0%BE%D1%80%D1%82%D1%80%D0%B5%D1%82)_2.jpg"><img alt="Денис Шмыгаль (портрет) 2.jpg" data-file-height="2048" data-file-width="1502" decoding="async" height="195" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e0/%D0%94%D0%B5%D0%BD%D0%B8%D1%81_%D0%A8%D0%BC%D1%8B%D0%B3%D0%B0%D0%BB%D1%8C_%28%D0%BF%D0%BE%D1%80%D1%82%D1%80%D0%B5%D1%82%29_2.jpg/143px-%D0%94%D0%B5%D0%BD%D0%B8%D1%81_%D0%A8%D0%BC%D1%8B%D0%B3%D0%B0%D0%BB%D1%8C_%28%D0%BF%D0%BE%D1%80%D1%82%D1%80%D0%B5%D1%82%29_2.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e0/%D0%94%D0%B5%D0%BD%D0%B8%D1%81_%D0%A8%D0%BC%D1%8B%D0%B3%D0%B0%D0%BB%D1%8C_%28%D0%BF%D0%BE%D1%80%D1%82%D1%80%D0%B5%D1%82%29_2.jpg/215px-%D0%94%D0%B5%D0%BD%D0%B8%D1%81_%D0%A8%D0%BC%D1%8B%D0%B3%D0%B0%D0%BB%D1%8C_%28%D0%BF%D0%BE%D1%80%D1%82%D1%80%D0%B5%D1%82%29_2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e0/%D0%94%D0%B5%D0%BD%D0%B8%D1%81_%D0%A8%D0%BC%D1%8B%D0%B3%D0%B0%D0%BB%D1%8C_%28%D0%BF%D0%BE%D1%80%D1%82%D1%80%D0%B5%D1%82%29_2.jpg/286px-%D0%94%D0%B5%D0%BD%D0%B8%D1%81_%D0%A8%D0%BC%D1%8B%D0%B3%D0%B0%D0%BB%D1%8C_%28%D0%BF%D0%BE%D1%80%D1%82%D1%80%D0%B5%D1%82%29_2.jpg 2x" width="143"/></a>
</td></tr>
<tr class="nowrap">
<td><a href="/wiki/Volodymyr_Zelenskyy" title="Volodymyr Zelenskyy">Volodymyr Zelenskyy</a><br/><small><a href="/wiki/President_of_Ukraine" title="President of Ukraine">President</a></small>
</td>
<td><a href="/wiki/Denys_Shmyhal" title="Denys Shmyhal">Denys Shmyhal</a><br/><small><a href="/wiki/Prime_Minister_of_Ukraine" title="Prime Minister of Ukraine">Prime Minister</a></small>
</td></tr></tbody></table>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/President_of_Ukraine" title="President of Ukraine">president</a> is elected by popular vote for a five-year term and is the formal <a href="/wiki/Head_of_state" title="Head of state">head of state</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-199"><a href="#cite_note-199">[194]</a></sup>
Ukraine's legislative branch includes the 450-seat <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Unicameral" title="Unicameral">unicameral</a> parliament, the <a href="/wiki/Verkhovna_Rada" title="Verkhovna Rada">Verkhovna Rada</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-200"><a href="#cite_note-200">[195]</a></sup> The parliament is primarily responsible for the formation of the executive branch and the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cabinet_of_Ministers_of_Ukraine" title="Cabinet of Ministers of Ukraine">Cabinet of Ministers</a>, headed by the <a href="/wiki/Prime_Minister_of_Ukraine" title="Prime Minister of Ukraine">prime minister</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-201"><a href="#cite_note-201">[196]</a></sup> The president retains the authority to nominate the ministers of foreign affairs and of defence for parliamentary approval, as well as the power to appoint the <a href="/wiki/Prosecutor_General_of_Ukraine" title="Prosecutor General of Ukraine">prosecutor general</a> and the head of the <a href="/wiki/Security_Service_of_Ukraine" title="Security Service of Ukraine">Security Service</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-202"><a href="#cite_note-202">[197]</a></sup>
</p><p>Laws, acts of the parliament and the cabinet, presidential decrees, and acts of the <a href="/wiki/Verkhovna_Rada_of_Crimea" title="Verkhovna Rada of Crimea">Crimean parliament</a> may be abrogated by the <a href="/wiki/Constitutional_Court_of_Ukraine" title="Constitutional Court of Ukraine">Constitutional Court</a>, should they be found to violate the constitution. Other normative acts are subject to judicial review. The <a href="/wiki/Supreme_Court_of_Ukraine" title="Supreme Court of Ukraine">Supreme Court</a> is the main body in the system of courts of general jurisdiction.
Local self-government is officially guaranteed. Local councils and city mayors are popularly elected and exercise control over local budgets. The heads of regional and district administrations are appointed by the president in accordance with the proposals of the prime minister.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-House2004_203-0"><a href="#cite_note-House2004-203">[198]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Courts_and_law_enforcement">Courts and law enforcement</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Judicial_system_of_Ukraine" title="Judicial system of Ukraine">Judicial system of Ukraine</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Law_enforcement_in_Ukraine" title="Law enforcement in Ukraine">Law enforcement in Ukraine</a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Klov_Palace._Listed_ID_80-382-0462._-_8_Pylypa_Orlyka_Street,_Pechersk_Raion,_Kiev._-_Pechersk_28_09_13_396.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2338" data-file-width="3900" decoding="async" height="132" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e1/Klov_Palace._Listed_ID_80-382-0462._-_8_Pylypa_Orlyka_Street%2C_Pechersk_Raion%2C_Kiev._-_Pechersk_28_09_13_396.jpg/220px-Klov_Palace._Listed_ID_80-382-0462._-_8_Pylypa_Orlyka_Street%2C_Pechersk_Raion%2C_Kiev._-_Pechersk_28_09_13_396.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e1/Klov_Palace._Listed_ID_80-382-0462._-_8_Pylypa_Orlyka_Street%2C_Pechersk_Raion%2C_Kiev._-_Pechersk_28_09_13_396.jpg/330px-Klov_Palace._Listed_ID_80-382-0462._-_8_Pylypa_Orlyka_Street%2C_Pechersk_Raion%2C_Kiev._-_Pechersk_28_09_13_396.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e1/Klov_Palace._Listed_ID_80-382-0462._-_8_Pylypa_Orlyka_Street%2C_Pechersk_Raion%2C_Kiev._-_Pechersk_28_09_13_396.jpg/440px-Klov_Palace._Listed_ID_80-382-0462._-_8_Pylypa_Orlyka_Street%2C_Pechersk_Raion%2C_Kiev._-_Pechersk_28_09_13_396.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Klov_Palace._Listed_ID_80-382-0462._-_8_Pylypa_Orlyka_Street,_Pechersk_Raion,_Kiev._-_Pechersk_28_09_13_396.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Klov_Palace" title="Klov Palace">Klovsky Palace</a>, home to the <a href="/wiki/Supreme_Court_of_Ukraine" title="Supreme Court of Ukraine">Supreme Court of Ukraine</a></div></div></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Martial_law_in_Ukraine" title="Martial law in Ukraine">Martial law</a> was declared when Russia invaded in February 2022,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-204"><a href="#cite_note-204">[199]</a></sup> and continues.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-205"><a href="#cite_note-205">[200]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-206"><a href="#cite_note-206">[201]</a></sup>
</p><p>The courts enjoy legal, financial and constitutional freedom guaranteed by Ukrainian law since 2002. Judges are largely well protected from dismissal (except for gross misconduct). Court justices are appointed by presidential decree for an initial period of five years, after which Ukraine's Supreme Council confirms their positions for life. Although there are still problems, the system is considered to have been much improved since Ukraine's independence in 1991. The Supreme Court is regarded as an independent and impartial body, and has on several occasions ruled against the Ukrainian government. The <a href="/wiki/World_Justice_Project" title="World Justice Project">World Justice Project</a> ranks Ukraine 66 out of 99 countries surveyed in its annual Rule of Law Index.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-207"><a href="#cite_note-207">[202]</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Prosecutor" title="Prosecutor">Prosecutors</a> in Ukraine have greater powers than in most European countries, and according to the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/European_Commission_for_Democracy_through_Law" title="European Commission for Democracy through Law">European Commission for Democracy through Law</a> "the role and functions of the Prosecutor's Office is not in accordance with <a href="/wiki/Council_of_Europe" title="Council of Europe">Council of Europe</a> standards".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-208"><a href="#cite_note-208">[203]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Conviction_rate" title="Conviction rate">conviction rate</a> is over 99%,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-209"><a href="#cite_note-209">[204]</a></sup> equal to the conviction rate of the <a href="/wiki/Soviet_Union" title="Soviet Union">Soviet Union</a>, with<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Moskal_210-0"><a href="#cite_note-Moskal-210">[205]</a></sup> suspects often being incarcerated for long periods before trial.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rotten_211-0"><a href="#cite_note-rotten-211">[206]</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:%D0%91%D1%83%D0%B4%D0%B8%D0%BD%D0%BE%D0%BA_%D1%83%D1%80%D1%8F%D0%B4%D1%83_%D0%A3%D0%BA%D1%80%D0%B0%D1%97%D0%BD%D0%B8,_%D0%9A%D0%B8%D1%97%D0%B2.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1944" data-file-width="2592" decoding="async" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/10/%D0%91%D1%83%D0%B4%D0%B8%D0%BD%D0%BE%D0%BA_%D1%83%D1%80%D1%8F%D0%B4%D1%83_%D0%A3%D0%BA%D1%80%D0%B0%D1%97%D0%BD%D0%B8%2C_%D0%9A%D0%B8%D1%97%D0%B2.JPG/220px-%D0%91%D1%83%D0%B4%D0%B8%D0%BD%D0%BE%D0%BA_%D1%83%D1%80%D1%8F%D0%B4%D1%83_%D0%A3%D0%BA%D1%80%D0%B0%D1%97%D0%BD%D0%B8%2C_%D0%9A%D0%B8%D1%97%D0%B2.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/10/%D0%91%D1%83%D0%B4%D0%B8%D0%BD%D0%BE%D0%BA_%D1%83%D1%80%D1%8F%D0%B4%D1%83_%D0%A3%D0%BA%D1%80%D0%B0%D1%97%D0%BD%D0%B8%2C_%D0%9A%D0%B8%D1%97%D0%B2.JPG/330px-%D0%91%D1%83%D0%B4%D0%B8%D0%BD%D0%BE%D0%BA_%D1%83%D1%80%D1%8F%D0%B4%D1%83_%D0%A3%D0%BA%D1%80%D0%B0%D1%97%D0%BD%D0%B8%2C_%D0%9A%D0%B8%D1%97%D0%B2.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/10/%D0%91%D1%83%D0%B4%D0%B8%D0%BD%D0%BE%D0%BA_%D1%83%D1%80%D1%8F%D0%B4%D1%83_%D0%A3%D0%BA%D1%80%D0%B0%D1%97%D0%BD%D0%B8%2C_%D0%9A%D0%B8%D1%97%D0%B2.JPG/440px-%D0%91%D1%83%D0%B4%D0%B8%D0%BD%D0%BE%D0%BA_%D1%83%D1%80%D1%8F%D0%B4%D1%83_%D0%A3%D0%BA%D1%80%D0%B0%D1%97%D0%BD%D0%B8%2C_%D0%9A%D0%B8%D1%97%D0%B2.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:%D0%91%D1%83%D0%B4%D0%B8%D0%BD%D0%BE%D0%BA_%D1%83%D1%80%D1%8F%D0%B4%D1%83_%D0%A3%D0%BA%D1%80%D0%B0%D1%97%D0%BD%D0%B8,_%D0%9A%D0%B8%D1%97%D0%B2.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Government_of_Ukraine" title="Government of Ukraine">Cabinet of Ministers</a> building</div></div></div>
<p>On 24 March 2010, <a href="/wiki/Viktor_Yanukovych" title="Viktor Yanukovych">President Yanukovych</a> formed an expert group to make recommendations on how to "clean up the current mess and adopt a law on court organization".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rotten_211-1"><a href="#cite_note-rotten-211">[206]</a></sup> One day later, he stated "We can no longer disgrace our country with such a court system."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rotten_211-2"><a href="#cite_note-rotten-211">[206]</a></sup> The criminal judicial system and the prison system of Ukraine remain quite punitive.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-United_States_Department_of_State_2021_212-0"><a href="#cite_note-United_States_Department_of_State_2021-212">[207]</a></sup>
</p><p>Since 2010 court proceedings can be held in Russian by mutual consent of the parties. Citizens unable to speak <a href="/wiki/Ukrainian_language" title="Ukrainian language">Ukrainian</a> or Russian may use their native language or the services of a translator.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-213"><a href="#cite_note-213">[208]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-214"><a href="#cite_note-214">[209]</a></sup> Previously all court proceedings had to be held in Ukrainian.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-United_States_Department_of_State_2021_212-1"><a href="#cite_note-United_States_Department_of_State_2021-212">[207]</a></sup>
</p><p>Law enforcement agencies are controlled by the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ministry_of_Internal_Affairs_of_Ukraine" title="Ministry of Internal Affairs of Ukraine">Ministry of Internal Affairs</a>. They consist primarily of the <a href="/wiki/National_Police_of_Ukraine" title="National Police of Ukraine">national police force</a> and various specialised units and agencies such as the <a href="/wiki/State_Border_Guard_Service_of_Ukraine" title="State Border Guard Service of Ukraine">State Border Guard</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Ukrainian_Sea_Guard" title="Ukrainian Sea Guard">Coast Guard</a> services. Law enforcement agencies, particularly the police, faced criticism for their heavy handling of the 2004 <a href="/wiki/Orange_Revolution" title="Orange Revolution">Orange Revolution</a>. Many thousands of police officers were stationed throughout the capital, primarily to dissuade protesters from challenging the state's authority but also to provide a quick reaction force in case of need; most officers were armed.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NYTSBU_215-0"><a href="#cite_note-NYTSBU-215">[210]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Foreign_relations">Foreign relations</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Foreign_relations_of_Ukraine" title="Foreign relations of Ukraine">Foreign relations of Ukraine</a>, <a href="/wiki/International_membership_of_Ukraine" title="International membership of Ukraine">International membership of Ukraine</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ukraine%E2%80%93European_Union_relations" title="Ukraine–European Union relations">Ukraine–European Union relations</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Ukraine_and_the_World_Bank" title="Ukraine and the World Bank">Ukraine and the World Bank</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Batumi_International_Conference,_on_19_July_2021_03_(cropped).jpg" title="File:Batumi International Conference, on 19 July 2021 03 (cropped).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1287" data-file-width="1931" decoding="async" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d4/Batumi_International_Conference%2C_on_19_July_2021_03_%28cropped%29.jpg/220px-Batumi_International_Conference%2C_on_19_July_2021_03_%28cropped%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d4/Batumi_International_Conference%2C_on_19_July_2021_03_%28cropped%29.jpg/330px-Batumi_International_Conference%2C_on_19_July_2021_03_%28cropped%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d4/Batumi_International_Conference%2C_on_19_July_2021_03_%28cropped%29.jpg/440px-Batumi_International_Conference%2C_on_19_July_2021_03_%28cropped%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Batumi_International_Conference,_on_19_July_2021_03_(cropped).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/President_of_Georgia" title="President of Georgia">President of Georgia</a> <a href="/wiki/Salome_Zourabichvili" title="Salome Zourabichvili">Salome Zurabishvili</a>, <a href="/wiki/President_of_Moldova" title="President of Moldova">President of Moldova</a> <a href="/wiki/Maia_Sandu" title="Maia Sandu">Maia Sandu</a>, <a href="/wiki/President_of_Ukraine" title="President of Ukraine">Ukrainian President</a> <a href="/wiki/Volodymyr_Zelenskyy" title="Volodymyr Zelenskyy">Volodymyr Zelenskyy</a> and <a href="/wiki/President_of_the_European_Council" title="President of the European Council">European Council President</a> <a href="/wiki/Charles_Michel" title="Charles Michel">Charles Michel</a> during the 2021 International Conference in <a href="/wiki/Batumi" title="Batumi">Batumi</a>. In 2014, the EU signed association agreements with all three countries.</div></div></div>
<p>From 1999 to 2001, Ukraine served as a non-permanent member of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/UN_Security_Council" title="UN Security Council">UN Security Council</a>. Historically, Soviet Ukraine joined the United Nations in 1945 as one of the original members following a Western compromise with the Soviet Union.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-U.S._Department_of_State,_Bureau_of_Public_Affairs,_Office_of_Public_Communication,_Editorial_Division.2000_216-0"><a href="#cite_note-U.S._Department_of_State,_Bureau_of_Public_Affairs,_Office_of_Public_Communication,_Editorial_Division.2000-216">[211]</a></sup> Ukraine has consistently supported peaceful, negotiated settlements to disputes. It has participated in the quadripartite talks on the conflict in Moldova and promoted a peaceful resolution to the conflict in the <a href="/wiki/Post-Soviet_states" title="Post-Soviet states">post-Soviet state</a> of Georgia. Ukraine also has made contributions to UN <a href="/wiki/Peacekeeping" title="Peacekeeping">peacekeeping</a> operations since 1992.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NATO_Information_Service._217-0"><a href="#cite_note-NATO_Information_Service.-217">[212]</a></sup>
</p><p>Ukraine considers Euro-Atlantic integration its primary foreign policy objective,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-result_of_Russia_218-0"><a href="#cite_note-result_of_Russia-218">[213]</a></sup> but in practice it has always balanced its relationship with the European Union and the United States with strong ties to Russia. The <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a>'s <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Partnership_and_Cooperation_Agreement" title="Partnership and Cooperation Agreement">Partnership and Cooperation Agreement</a> (PCA) with Ukraine went into force in 1998. The European Union (EU) has encouraged Ukraine to implement the PCA fully before discussions begin on an association agreement, issued at the EU Summit in December 1999 in <a href="/wiki/Helsinki" title="Helsinki">Helsinki</a>, recognizes Ukraine's long-term aspirations but does not discuss association.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-result_of_Russia_218-1"><a href="#cite_note-result_of_Russia-218">[213]</a></sup>
</p><p>In 1992, Ukraine joined the then-Conference on Security and Cooperation in Europe (now the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Organization_for_Security_and_Cooperation_in_Europe" title="Organization for Security and Cooperation in Europe">Organization for Security and Cooperation in Europe</a> (OSCE)), and also became a member of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/North_Atlantic_Cooperation_Council" title="North Atlantic Cooperation Council">North Atlantic Cooperation Council</a>. <a href="/wiki/Ukraine%E2%80%93NATO_relations" title="Ukraine–NATO relations">Ukraine–NATO relations</a> are close and the country has declared interest in eventual membership.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-result_of_Russia_218-2"><a href="#cite_note-result_of_Russia-218">[213]</a></sup>
</p><p>Ukraine is the most active member of the <a href="/wiki/Partnership_for_Peace" title="Partnership for Peace">Partnership for Peace</a> (PfP). All major political parties in Ukraine support full eventual integration into the European Union.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-219"><a href="#cite_note-219">[214]</a></sup> The Association Agreement between Ukraine and the European Union was signed in 2014.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-220"><a href="#cite_note-220">[215]</a></sup>
</p><p>
Ukraine long had close ties with all its neighbours, but <a href="/wiki/Russia%E2%80%93Ukraine_relations" title="Russia–Ukraine relations">Russia–Ukraine relations</a> rapidly deteriorated in 2014 due to the <a href="/wiki/Annexation_of_Crimea_by_the_Russian_Federation" title="Annexation of Crimea by the Russian Federation">annexation of Crimea</a>, energy dependence and payment disputes. </p><div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:EU_DCFTA_EFTA.svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="520" data-file-width="680" decoding="async" height="168" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7e/EU_DCFTA_EFTA.svg/220px-EU_DCFTA_EFTA.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7e/EU_DCFTA_EFTA.svg/330px-EU_DCFTA_EFTA.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7e/EU_DCFTA_EFTA.svg/440px-EU_DCFTA_EFTA.svg.png 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:EU_DCFTA_EFTA.svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>In January 2016, Ukraine joined the <a href="/wiki/Deep_and_Comprehensive_Free_Trade_Area" title="Deep and Comprehensive Free Trade Area">Deep and Comprehensive Free Trade Area</a> (green) with the EU (blue), established by the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ukraine%E2%80%93European_Union_Association_Agreement" title="Ukraine–European Union Association Agreement">Ukraine–European Union Association Agreement</a>, opening its path towards <a href="/wiki/European_integration" title="European integration">European integration</a>.</div></div></div><p>The <a href="/wiki/Deep_and_Comprehensive_Free_Trade_Area" title="Deep and Comprehensive Free Trade Area">Deep and Comprehensive Free Trade Area</a> (DCFTA), which entered into force in January 2016 following the ratification of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ukraine%E2%80%93European_Union_Association_Agreement" title="Ukraine–European Union Association Agreement">Ukraine–European Union Association Agreement</a>, formally integrates Ukraine into the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/European_Single_Market" title="European Single Market">European Single Market</a> and the <a href="/wiki/European_Economic_Area" title="European Economic Area">European Economic Area</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-221"><a href="#cite_note-221">[216]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-222"><a href="#cite_note-222">[217]</a></sup> Ukraine receives further support and assistance for its <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Future_enlargement_of_the_European_Union" title="Future enlargement of the European Union">EU-accession</a> aspirations from the International Visegrád Fund of the <a href="/wiki/Visegr%C3%A1d_Group" title="Visegrád Group">Visegrád Group</a> that consists of <a href="/wiki/Central_Europe" title="Central Europe">Central European</a> <a href="/wiki/Member_state_of_the_European_Union" title="Member state of the European Union">EU members</a> the Czech Republic, Poland, Hungary and Slovakia.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-223"><a href="#cite_note-223">[218]</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2020, in <a href="/wiki/Lublin" title="Lublin">Lublin</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lithuania" title="Lithuania">Lithuania</a>, Poland and Ukraine created the <a href="/wiki/Lublin_Triangle" title="Lublin Triangle">Lublin Triangle</a> initiative, which aims to create further cooperation between the three historical countries of the <a href="/wiki/Polish%E2%80%93Lithuanian_Commonwealth" title="Polish–Lithuanian Commonwealth">Polish–Lithuanian Commonwealth</a> and further Ukraine's integration and accession to the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/EU" title="EU">EU</a> and <a href="/wiki/NATO" title="NATO">NATO</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-224"><a href="#cite_note-224">[219]</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2021, the <a href="/wiki/Association_Trio" title="Association Trio">Association Trio</a> was formed by signing a joint memorandum between the <a href="/wiki/Ministry_of_Foreign_Affairs_of_Georgia" title="Ministry of Foreign Affairs of Georgia">Foreign Ministers of Georgia</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ministry_of_Foreign_Affairs_and_European_Integration_of_Moldova" title="Ministry of Foreign Affairs and European Integration of Moldova">Moldova</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ministry_of_Foreign_Affairs_(Ukraine)" title="Ministry of Foreign Affairs (Ukraine)">Ukraine</a>. The Association Trio is a tripartite format for enhanced cooperation, coordination, and dialogue between the three countries (that have signed the Association Agreement with the EU) with the <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a> on issues of common interest related to <a href="/wiki/European_integration" title="European integration">European integration</a>, enhancing cooperation within the framework of the <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Partnership" title="Eastern Partnership">Eastern Partnership</a>, and committing to the prospect of joining the European Union.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-225"><a href="#cite_note-225">[220]</a></sup> As of 2021, Ukraine was preparing to formally apply for <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">EU</a> membership in 2024, in order to join the European Union in the 2030s,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:1_226-0"><a href="#cite_note-:1-226">[221]</a></sup> however, with the Russian invasion of Ukraine in 2022, Ukrainian president Volodymyr Zelenskyy requested that the country be admitted to the EU immediately.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-auto1_227-0"><a href="#cite_note-auto1-227">[222]</a></sup> Candidate status was granted on 23 June 2022.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BBC_News_172-1"><a href="#cite_note-BBC_News-172">[167]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Armed_forces">Armed forces</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Armed_Forces_of_Ukraine" title="Armed Forces of Ukraine">Armed Forces of Ukraine</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Kissing_the_flag.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="810" data-file-width="1090" decoding="async" height="163" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f7/Kissing_the_flag.jpg/220px-Kissing_the_flag.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f7/Kissing_the_flag.jpg/330px-Kissing_the_flag.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f7/Kissing_the_flag.jpg/440px-Kissing_the_flag.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Kissing_the_flag.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Henadii Lachkov, commander of the Ukrainian contingent in <a href="/wiki/Multi-National_Force_%E2%80%93_Iraq" title="Multi-National Force – Iraq">Multi-National Force – Iraq</a>, kissing his country's flag</div></div></div>
<p>After the dissolution of the Soviet Union, Ukraine inherited a 780,000-man military force on its territory, equipped with the third-largest <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nuclear_weapons_and_Ukraine" title="Nuclear weapons and Ukraine">nuclear weapons arsenal</a> in the world.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-milgov_228-0"><a href="#cite_note-milgov-228">[223]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-229"><a href="#cite_note-229">[224]</a></sup> In 1992, Ukraine signed the <a href="/wiki/Lisbon_Protocol" title="Lisbon Protocol">Lisbon Protocol</a> in which the country agreed to give up all nuclear weapons to Russia for disposal and to join the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nuclear_Non-Proliferation_Treaty" title="Nuclear Non-Proliferation Treaty">Nuclear Non-Proliferation Treaty</a> as a non-nuclear weapon state. By 1996 the country had become free of nuclear weapons.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-milgov_228-1"><a href="#cite_note-milgov-228">[223]</a></sup>
</p><p>Ukraine took consistent steps toward reduction of conventional weapons. It signed the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_on_Conventional_Armed_Forces_in_Europe" title="Treaty on Conventional Armed Forces in Europe">Treaty on Conventional Armed Forces in Europe</a>, which called for reduction of tanks, artillery, and armoured vehicles (army forces were reduced to 300,000). The country plans to convert the current <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Conscript" title="Conscript">conscript</a>-based military into a professional <a href="/wiki/Volunteer_military" title="Volunteer military">volunteer military</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-wbook06_230-0"><a href="#cite_note-wbook06-230">[225]</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template noprint noexcerpt Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Wikipedia:NOTRS" title="Wikipedia:NOTRS"><span title="old (March 2022)">better source needed</span></a></i>]</sup> Ukraine's current military consist of 196,600 active personnel and around 900,000 reservists.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-231"><a href="#cite_note-231">[226]</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Ukrainian_navy_frigate_Hetman_Sahaydachniy_(26743398421).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="639" data-file-width="960" decoding="async" height="146" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d0/Ukrainian_navy_frigate_Hetman_Sahaydachniy_%2826743398421%29.jpg/220px-Ukrainian_navy_frigate_Hetman_Sahaydachniy_%2826743398421%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d0/Ukrainian_navy_frigate_Hetman_Sahaydachniy_%2826743398421%29.jpg/330px-Ukrainian_navy_frigate_Hetman_Sahaydachniy_%2826743398421%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d0/Ukrainian_navy_frigate_Hetman_Sahaydachniy_%2826743398421%29.jpg/440px-Ukrainian_navy_frigate_Hetman_Sahaydachniy_%2826743398421%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Ukrainian_navy_frigate_Hetman_Sahaydachniy_(26743398421).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The Ukrainian frigate <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hetman_Sahaydachniy_(U130)" title="Hetman Sahaydachniy (U130)"><i>Hetman Sahaydachniy</i> (U130)</a></div></div></div>
<p>Ukraine played an increasing role in peacekeeping operations. In 2014, the Ukrainian frigate <i>Hetman Sagaidachniy</i> joined the European Union's counter piracy <a href="/wiki/Operation_Atalanta" title="Operation Atalanta">Operation Atalanta</a> and was part of the EU Naval Force off the coast of <a href="/wiki/Somalia" title="Somalia">Somalia</a> for two months.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-232"><a href="#cite_note-232">[227]</a></sup> Ukrainian troops were deployed in <a href="/wiki/Kosovo" title="Kosovo">Kosovo</a> as part of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Polish-Ukrainian_Peace_Force_Battalion" title="Polish-Ukrainian Peace Force Battalion">Ukrainian-Polish Battalion</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-233"><a href="#cite_note-233">[228]</a></sup>
</p><p>A Ukrainian unit was deployed in <a href="/wiki/Lebanon" title="Lebanon">Lebanon</a>, as part of <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Interim_Force_in_Lebanon" title="United Nations Interim Force in Lebanon">UN Interim Force</a> enforcing the mandated ceasefire agreement. There was also a maintenance and training battalion deployed in <a href="/wiki/Sierra_Leone" title="Sierra Leone">Sierra Leone</a>. In 2003–05, a Ukrainian unit was deployed as part of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Multinational_force_in_Iraq" title="Multinational force in Iraq">multinational force in Iraq</a> under Polish command.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-234"><a href="#cite_note-234">[229]</a></sup>
</p><p>Military units of other states participated in multinational military exercises with Ukrainian forces in Ukraine regularly, including <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/U.S._military" title="U.S. military">U.S. military</a> forces.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-235"><a href="#cite_note-235">[230]</a></sup>
</p><p>Following independence, Ukraine declared itself a neutral state.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-gska2.rada.gov.ua_20-1"><a href="#cite_note-gska2.rada.gov.ua-20">[15]</a></sup> The country had a limited military partnership with Russian Federation and other CIS countries and has had a <a href="/wiki/Partnership_for_Peace" title="Partnership for Peace">partnership with NATO</a> since 1994. In the 2000s, the government was leaning towards NATO, and deeper cooperation with the alliance was set by the NATO-Ukraine Action Plan signed in 2002. It was later agreed that the question of joining NATO should be answered by a national referendum at some point in the future.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-wbook06_230-1"><a href="#cite_note-wbook06-230">[225]</a></sup> Deposed <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ukrainian_President" title="Ukrainian President">President</a> <a href="/wiki/Viktor_Yanukovych" title="Viktor Yanukovych">Viktor Yanukovych</a> considered the current level of co-operation between <a href="/wiki/Ukraine%E2%80%93NATO_relations" title="Ukraine–NATO relations">Ukraine and NATO</a> sufficient, and was against Ukraine joining NATO. During the <a href="/wiki/2008_Bucharest_summit" title="2008 Bucharest summit">2008 Bucharest summit</a>, NATO declared that Ukraine would eventually become a member of NATO when it meets the criteria for accession.
</p><p>As part of modernization after the beginning of the <a href="/wiki/Russo-Ukrainian_War" title="Russo-Ukrainian War">Russo-Ukrainian War</a> in 2014, junior officers were allowed to take more initiative and a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Territorial_defence_battalions_(Ukraine)" title="Territorial defence battalions (Ukraine)">territorial defense force</a> of volunteers was established.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-236"><a href="#cite_note-236">[231]</a></sup> Various defensive weapons including <a href="/wiki/Unmanned_combat_aerial_vehicle" title="Unmanned combat aerial vehicle">drones</a> were supplied by many countries, but not fighter jets.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-237"><a href="#cite_note-237">[232]</a></sup> During the first few weeks of the <a href="/wiki/2022_Russian_invasion_of_Ukraine" title="2022 Russian invasion of Ukraine">2022 Russian invasion</a> the military found it difficult to defend against shelling, missiles and high level bombing; but light infantry used shoulder-mounted weapons effectively to destroy tanks, armoured vehicles and low-flying aircraft.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-238"><a href="#cite_note-238">[233]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Administrative_divisions">Administrative divisions</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Administrative_divisions_of_Ukraine" title="Administrative divisions of Ukraine">Administrative divisions of Ukraine</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ukrainian_historical_regions" title="Ukrainian historical regions">Ukrainian historical regions</a></div>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Further information: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Political_status_of_Crimea_and_Sevastopol" title="Political status of Crimea and Sevastopol">Political status of Crimea and Sevastopol</a> and <a href="/wiki/Annexation_of_Crimea_by_the_Russian_Federation" title="Annexation of Crimea by the Russian Federation">Annexation of Crimea by the Russian Federation</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:352px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Map_of_Ukraine_with_Cities.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3255" data-file-width="4844" decoding="async" height="235" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3f/Map_of_Ukraine_with_Cities.png/350px-Map_of_Ukraine_with_Cities.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3f/Map_of_Ukraine_with_Cities.png/525px-Map_of_Ukraine_with_Cities.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3f/Map_of_Ukraine_with_Cities.png/700px-Map_of_Ukraine_with_Cities.png 2x" width="350"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Map_of_Ukraine_with_Cities.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Ukraine (2021) — major cities and adjacent countries</div></div></div>
<p>The system of Ukrainian subdivisions reflects the country's status as a <a href="/wiki/Unitary_state" title="Unitary state">unitary state</a> (as stated in the country's constitution) with unified legal and <a href="/wiki/Local_government" title="Local government">administrative</a> regimes for each unit.
</p><p>Including Sevastopol and the Autonomous Republic of Crimea that were annexed by the Russian Federation in 2014, Ukraine consists of 27 regions: twenty-four <a href="/wiki/Oblast" title="Oblast">oblasts</a> (provinces), one <a href="/wiki/Autonomous_republic" title="Autonomous republic">autonomous republic</a> (<a href="/wiki/Autonomous_Republic_of_Crimea" title="Autonomous Republic of Crimea">Autonomous Republic of Crimea</a>), and two cities of special status—<a href="/wiki/Kyiv" title="Kyiv">Kyiv</a>, the capital, and <a href="/wiki/Sevastopol" title="Sevastopol">Sevastopol</a>. The 24 oblasts and Crimea are subdivided into 136<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-239"><a href="#cite_note-239">[234]</a></sup> <span title="Ukrainian-language text"><i lang="uk-Latn"><a href="/wiki/Raion" title="Raion">raions</a></i></span> (districts) and city municipalities of regional significance, or second-level administrative units.
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Populated_places_in_Ukraine" title="Populated places in Ukraine">Populated places in Ukraine</a> are split into two categories: urban and rural. Urban populated places are split further into cities and <a href="/wiki/Urban-type_settlement" title="Urban-type settlement">urban-type settlements</a> (a Soviet administrative invention), while rural populated places consist of villages and settlements (a generally used term). All cities have a certain degree of self-rule depending on their significance such as national significance (as in the case of Kyiv and Sevastopol), regional significance (within each oblast or autonomous republic) or district significance (all the rest of cities). A city's significance depends on several factors such as its population, socio-economic and historical importance and infrastructure.
</p>

//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/af/%D0%9C%D1%96%D1%81%D1%82_%D0%9F%D0%B0%D1%82%D0%BE%D0%BD%D0%B0_%D0%B7_%D0%BD%D1%96%D1%87%D0%BD%D0%BE%D1%8E_%D0%B0%D1%80%D1%85%D1%96%D1%82%D0%B5%D0%BA%D1%82%D1%83%D1%80%D0%BD%D0%BE%D1%8E_%D0%BF%D1%96%D0%B4%D1%81%D0%B2%D1%96%D1%82%D0%BA%D0%BE%D1%8E_%D1%82%D0%B0_%D0%BF%D0%B0%D0%BD%D0%BE%D1%80%D0%B0%D0%BC%D0%B0_%D0%9B%D1%96%D0%B2%D0%BE%D0%B3%D0%BE_%D0%B1%D0%B5%D1%80%D0%B5%D0%B3%D0%B0.jpg/440px-%D0%9C%D1%96%D1%81%D1%82_%D0%9F%D0%B0%D1%82%D0%BE%D0%BD%D0%B0_%D0%B7_%D0%BD%D1%96%D1%87%D0%BD%D0%BE%D1%8E_%D0%B0%D1%80%D1%85%D1%96%D1%82%D0%B5%D0%BA%D1%82%D1%83%D1%80%D0%BD%D0%BE%D1%8E_%D0%BF%D1%96%D0%B4%D1%81%D0%B2%D1%96%D1%82%D0%BA%D0%BE%D1%8E_%D1%82%D0%B0_%D0%BF%D0%B0%D0%BD%D0%BE%D1%80%D0%B0%D0%BC%D0%B0_%D0%9B%D1%96%D0%B2%D0%BE%D0%B3%D0%BE_%D0%B1%D0%B5%D1%80%D0%B5%D0%B3%D0%B0.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:%D0%9C%D1%96%D1%81%D1%82_%D0%9F%D0%B0%D1%82%D0%BE%D0%BD%D0%B0_%D0%B7_%D0%BD%D1%96%D1%87%D0%BD%D0%BE%D1%8E_%D0%B0%D1%80%D1%85%D1%96%D1%82%D0%B5%D0%BA%D1%82%D1%83%D1%80%D0%BD%D0%BE%D1%8E_%D0%BF%D1%96%D0%B4%D1%81%D0%B2%D1%96%D1%82%D0%BA%D0%BE%D1%8E_%D1%82%D0%B0_%D0%BF%D0%B0%D0%BD%D0%BE%D1%80%D0%B0%D0%BC%D0%B0_%D0%9B%D1%96%D0%B2%D0%BE%D0%B3%D0%BE_%D0%B1%D0%B5%D1%80%D0%B5%D0%B3%D0%B0.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Kyiv" title="Kyiv">Kyiv</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Financial_centre" title="Financial centre">financial centre</a> of Ukraine</div></div></div>
<p>In 2021 agriculture was the biggest sector of the economy and Ukraine was the world's largest <a href="/wiki/Grain_trade" title="Grain trade">wheat exporter</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:4_240-0"><a href="#cite_note-:4-240">[235]</a></sup> However, Ukraine remains among the <a href="/wiki/List_of_sovereign_states_in_Europe_by_GDP_(nominal)_per_capita" title="List of sovereign states in Europe by GDP (nominal) per capita">poorest countries in Europe</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-poor_241-0"><a href="#cite_note-poor-241">[236]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Corruption_in_Ukraine" title="Corruption in Ukraine">corruption remains a widespread issue</a>; the country was rated 122nd out of 180 in the <a href="/wiki/Corruption_Perceptions_Index" title="Corruption Perceptions Index">Corruption Perceptions Index</a> for 2021, the second-lowest result in Europe after <a href="/wiki/Corruption_in_Russia" title="Corruption in Russia">Russia</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sec_242-0"><a href="#cite_note-sec-242">[237]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-transparency_243-0"><a href="#cite_note-transparency-243">[238]</a></sup> In 2021 Ukraine's <a href="/wiki/Gross_domestic_product" title="Gross domestic product">GDP</a> per capita by <a href="/wiki/Purchasing_power_parity" title="Purchasing power parity">purchasing power parity</a> was just over $14,000.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-244"><a href="#cite_note-244">[239]</a></sup> Despite supplying <a href="/wiki/List_of_foreign_aid_to_Ukraine_during_the_Russo-Ukrainian_War" title="List of foreign aid to Ukraine during the Russo-Ukrainian War">emergency financial support</a>, the <a href="/wiki/International_Monetary_Fund" title="International Monetary Fund">IMF</a> expected the economy to shrink considerably in 2022 due to <a href="/wiki/2022_Russian_invasion_of_Ukraine" title="2022 Russian invasion of Ukraine">Russia's invasion</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-auto4_245-0"><a href="#cite_note-auto4-245">[240]</a></sup> One 2022 estimate was that post-war reconstruction costs might reach half a trillion dollars.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-246"><a href="#cite_note-246">[241]</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2021, the average salary in Ukraine reached its highest level at almost <a href="/wiki/Ukrainian_hryvnia" title="Ukrainian hryvnia">₴</a>14,300 (US$525) per month.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-247"><a href="#cite_note-247">[242]</a></sup> About 1% of Ukrainians lived <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Poverty_by_country" title="Poverty by country">below the national poverty line</a> in 2019.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-248"><a href="#cite_note-248">[243]</a></sup> Unemployment in Ukraine was 4.5% in 2019.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-249"><a href="#cite_note-249">[244]</a></sup> In 2019 5–15% of the Ukrainian population were categorized as middle class.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-250"><a href="#cite_note-250">[245]</a></sup> In 2020 Ukraine's <a href="/wiki/Government_debt" title="Government debt">government debt</a> was roughly 50% of its nominal GDP.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-251"><a href="#cite_note-251">[246]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:4_240-1"><a href="#cite_note-:4-240">[235]</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2021 mineral commodities and light industry were important sectors.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:4_240-2"><a href="#cite_note-:4-240">[235]</a></sup> Ukraine produces nearly all types of transportation vehicles and <a href="/wiki/State_Space_Agency_of_Ukraine" title="State Space Agency of Ukraine">spacecraft</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-252"><a href="#cite_note-252">[247]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-253"><a href="#cite_note-253">[248]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-254"><a href="#cite_note-254">[249]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Antonov" title="Antonov">Antonov</a> airplanes and <a href="/wiki/KrAZ" title="KrAZ">KrAZ</a> trucks are exported to many countries. The <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a> is the country's main trade partner, and remittances from Ukrainians working abroad are important.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:4_240-3"><a href="#cite_note-:4-240">[235]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Agriculture">Agriculture</span></h3>
<p>Ukraine is among the world's top agricultural producers and exporters and is often described as the "bread basket of Europe". During the 2020/21 international wheat marketing season (July–June), it ranked as the sixth largest wheat exporter, accounting for nine percent of world wheat trade.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:02_255-0"><a href="#cite_note-:02-255">[250]</a></sup> The country is also a major global exporter of maize, barley and rapeseed. In 2020/21, it accounted for 12 percent of global trade in <a href="/wiki/Maize" title="Maize">maize</a> and <a href="/wiki/Barley" title="Barley">barley</a> and for 14 percent of world <a href="/wiki/Rapeseed" title="Rapeseed">rapeseed</a> exports. Its trade share is even greater in the sunflower oil sector, with the country accounting for about 50 percent of world exports in 2020/2021.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:02_255-1"><a href="#cite_note-:02-255">[250]</a></sup>
</p><p>According to the <a href="/wiki/Food_and_Agriculture_Organization" title="Food and Agriculture Organization">Food and Agriculture Organization of the United Nations</a> (FAO), further to causing the loss of lives and increasing humanitarian needs, the likely disruptions caused by the <a href="/wiki/Russo-Ukrainian_War" title="Russo-Ukrainian War">Russo-Ukrainian War</a> to Ukraine's grain and oilseed sectors, could jeopardize the food security of many countries, especially those that are highly dependent on Ukraine and Russia for their food and fertilizer imports.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-256"><a href="#cite_note-256">[251]</a></sup> Several of these countries fall into the <a href="/wiki/Least_developed_countries" title="Least developed countries">Least Developed Country</a> (LDC) group, while many others belong to the group of <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Low-Income_Food-Deficit_Countries&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Low-Income Food-Deficit Countries (page does not exist)">Low-Income Food-Deficit Countries</a> (LIFDCs).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-257"><a href="#cite_note-257">[252]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-258"><a href="#cite_note-258">[253]</a></sup> For example <a href="/wiki/Eritrea" title="Eritrea">Eritrea</a> sourced 47 percent of its wheat imports in 2021 from Ukraine. Overall, more than 30 nations depend on Ukraine and the Russian Federation for over 30 percent of their wheat import needs, many of them in North Africa and Western and Central Asia.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:02_255-2"><a href="#cite_note-:02-255">[250]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Tourism">Tourism</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Tourism_in_Ukraine" title="Tourism in Ukraine">Tourism in Ukraine</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:%D0%97%D0%B8%D0%BC%D0%BE%D0%B2%D0%B0_%D1%84%D0%BE%D1%80%D1%82%D0%B5%D1%86%D1%8F.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2500" data-file-width="3755" decoding="async" height="146" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a0/%D0%97%D0%B8%D0%BC%D0%BE%D0%B2%D0%B0_%D1%84%D0%BE%D1%80%D1%82%D0%B5%D1%86%D1%8F.jpg/220px-%D0%97%D0%B8%D0%BC%D0%BE%D0%B2%D0%B0_%D1%84%D0%BE%D1%80%D1%82%D0%B5%D1%86%D1%8F.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a0/%D0%97%D0%B8%D0%BC%D0%BE%D0%B2%D0%B0_%D1%84%D0%BE%D1%80%D1%82%D0%B5%D1%86%D1%8F.jpg/330px-%D0%97%D0%B8%D0%BC%D0%BE%D0%B2%D0%B0_%D1%84%D0%BE%D1%80%D1%82%D0%B5%D1%86%D1%8F.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a0/%D0%97%D0%B8%D0%BC%D0%BE%D0%B2%D0%B0_%D1%84%D0%BE%D1%80%D1%82%D0%B5%D1%86%D1%8F.jpg/440px-%D0%97%D0%B8%D0%BC%D0%BE%D0%B2%D0%B0_%D1%84%D0%BE%D1%80%D1%82%D0%B5%D1%86%D1%8F.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:%D0%97%D0%B8%D0%BC%D0%BE%D0%B2%D0%B0_%D1%84%D0%BE%D1%80%D1%82%D0%B5%D1%86%D1%8F.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Kamianets-Podilskyi_Castle" title="Kamianets-Podilskyi Castle">Kamianets-Podilskyi Castle</a>, one of the <a href="/wiki/Seven_Wonders_of_Ukraine" title="Seven Wonders of Ukraine">Seven Wonders of Ukraine</a></div></div></div>
<p>Before the <a href="/wiki/Russo-Ukrainian_War" title="Russo-Ukrainian War">Russo-Ukrainian war</a> the number of tourists visiting Ukraine was eighth in Europe, according to the <a href="/wiki/World_Tourism_Organization" title="World Tourism Organization">World Tourism Organization</a> <a href="/wiki/World_Tourism_rankings" title="World Tourism rankings">rankings</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-259"><a href="#cite_note-259">[254]</a></sup> Ukraine has numerous tourist attractions: mountain ranges suitable for <a href="/wiki/Skiing" title="Skiing">skiing</a>, hiking and fishing; the <a href="/wiki/Black_Sea" title="Black Sea">Black Sea</a> coastline as a popular summer destination; <a href="/wiki/Nature_reserve" title="Nature reserve">nature reserves</a> of different <a href="/wiki/Ecosystem" title="Ecosystem">ecosystems</a>; and churches, <a href="/wiki/Castle" title="Castle">castle</a> ruins and other architectural and park landmarks. <a href="/wiki/Kyiv" title="Kyiv">Kyiv</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lviv" title="Lviv">Lviv</a>, <a href="/wiki/Odesa" title="Odesa">Odesa</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kamyanets-Podilskyi" title="Kamyanets-Podilskyi">Kamyanets-Podilskyi</a> were Ukraine's principal tourist centres, each offering many historical landmarks and extensive <a href="/wiki/Hospitality" title="Hospitality">hospitality</a> infrastructure. The <a href="/wiki/Seven_Wonders_of_Ukraine" title="Seven Wonders of Ukraine">Seven Wonders of Ukraine</a> and <a href="/wiki/Seven_Natural_Wonders_of_Ukraine" title="Seven Natural Wonders of Ukraine">Seven Natural Wonders of Ukraine</a> are selections of the most important landmarks of Ukraine, chosen by Ukrainian experts and an Internet-based public vote. Tourism was the mainstay of Crimea's economy before a major fall in visitor numbers following the Russian annexation in 2014.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-260"><a href="#cite_note-260">[255]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Transport">Transport</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Transport_in_Ukraine" title="Transport in Ukraine">Transport in Ukraine</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:%D0%A1%D0%BA%D0%BE%D1%80%D0%BE%D1%81%D1%82%D0%BD%D0%BE%D0%B9_%D0%BF%D0%BE%D0%B5%D0%B7%D0%B4_%22%D0%A5%D0%B5%D0%BD%D0%B4%D0%B0%D0%B9%22.jpg"><img alt="HRCS2 unit" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1611" data-file-width="2232" decoding="async" height="159" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4d/%D0%A1%D0%BA%D0%BE%D1%80%D0%BE%D1%81%D1%82%D0%BD%D0%BE%D0%B9_%D0%BF%D0%BE%D0%B5%D0%B7%D0%B4_%22%D0%A5%D0%B5%D0%BD%D0%B4%D0%B0%D0%B9%22.jpg/220px-%D0%A1%D0%BA%D0%BE%D1%80%D0%BE%D1%81%D1%82%D0%BD%D0%BE%D0%B9_%D0%BF%D0%BE%D0%B5%D0%B7%D0%B4_%22%D0%A5%D0%B5%D0%BD%D0%B4%D0%B0%D0%B9%22.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4d/%D0%A1%D0%BA%D0%BE%D1%80%D0%BE%D1%81%D1%82%D0%BD%D0%BE%D0%B9_%D0%BF%D0%BE%D0%B5%D0%B7%D0%B4_%22%D0%A5%D0%B5%D0%BD%D0%B4%D0%B0%D0%B9%22.jpg/330px-%D0%A1%D0%BA%D0%BE%D1%80%D0%BE%D1%81%D1%82%D0%BD%D0%BE%D0%B9_%D0%BF%D0%BE%D0%B5%D0%B7%D0%B4_%22%D0%A5%D0%B5%D0%BD%D0%B4%D0%B0%D0%B9%22.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4d/%D0%A1%D0%BA%D0%BE%D1%80%D0%BE%D1%81%D1%82%D0%BD%D0%BE%D0%B9_%D0%BF%D0%BE%D0%B5%D0%B7%D0%B4_%22%D0%A5%D0%B5%D0%BD%D0%B4%D0%B0%D0%B9%22.jpg/440px-%D0%A1%D0%BA%D0%BE%D1%80%D0%BE%D1%81%D1%82%D0%BD%D0%BE%D0%B9_%D0%BF%D0%BE%D0%B5%D0%B7%D0%B4_%22%D0%A5%D0%B5%D0%BD%D0%B4%D0%B0%D0%B9%22.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:%D0%A1%D0%BA%D0%BE%D1%80%D0%BE%D1%81%D1%82%D0%BD%D0%BE%D0%B9_%D0%BF%D0%BE%D0%B5%D0%B7%D0%B4_%22%D0%A5%D0%B5%D0%BD%D0%B4%D0%B0%D0%B9%22.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/HRCS2_multiple_unit" title="HRCS2 multiple unit">HRCS2 multiple unit</a>. <a href="/wiki/Ukrainian_Railways" title="Ukrainian Railways">Rail transport</a> is heavily utilised in Ukraine.</div></div></div>
<p>Many roads and bridges were destroyed, and international maritime travel was blocked by the 2022 Russian invasion of Ukraine.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-auto4_245-1"><a href="#cite_note-auto4-245">[240]</a></sup> Before that it was mainly through the <a href="/wiki/Port_of_Odesa" title="Port of Odesa">Port of Odesa</a>, from where ferries sailed regularly to <a href="/wiki/Istanbul" title="Istanbul">Istanbul</a>, <a href="/wiki/Varna,_Bulgaria" title="Varna, Bulgaria">Varna</a> and <a href="/wiki/Haifa" title="Haifa">Haifa</a>. The largest ferry company operating these routes was <a href="/wiki/UkrFerry" title="UkrFerry">Ukrferry</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-261"><a href="#cite_note-261">[256]</a></sup> There are over 1,600 km (1,000 mi) of <a href="/wiki/Navigability" title="Navigability">navigable</a> waterways on 7 rivers, mostly on the <a href="/wiki/Danube" title="Danube">Danube</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dnieper" title="Dnieper">Dnieper</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pripyat_River" title="Pripyat River">Pripyat</a>. All Ukraine's rivers freeze over in winter, limiting navigation.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-262"><a href="#cite_note-262">[257]</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Rail_transport_in_Ukraine" title="Rail transport in Ukraine">Ukraine's rail network</a> connects all major urban areas, port facilities and <a href="/wiki/Manufacturing" title="Manufacturing">industrial centres</a> with neighbouring countries.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="Seems unlikely in the middle of a war (July 2022)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> The heaviest concentration of <a href="/wiki/Railway_track" title="Railway track">railway track</a> is the <a href="/wiki/Donbas" title="Donbas">Donbas</a> region.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-263"><a href="#cite_note-263">[258]</a></sup> Although <a href="/wiki/Rail_freight_transport" title="Rail freight transport">rail freight transport</a> fell in the 1990s, Ukraine is still one of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rail_usage_statistics_by_country" title="Rail usage statistics by country">world's highest rail users</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-264"><a href="#cite_note-264">[259]</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Ukraine_International_Airlines" title="Ukraine International Airlines">Ukraine International Airlines</a>, is the <a href="/wiki/Flag_carrier" title="Flag carrier">flag carrier</a> and the largest <a href="/wiki/Airline" title="Airline">airline</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-265"><a href="#cite_note-265">[260]</a></sup> with its head office in <a href="/wiki/Kyiv" title="Kyiv">Kyiv</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-266"><a href="#cite_note-266">[261]</a></sup> and its main hub at Kyiv's <a href="/wiki/Boryspil_International_Airport" title="Boryspil International Airport">Boryspil International Airport</a>. It operated domestic and international passenger flights and cargo services to Europe, the Middle East, the United States,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-auto1_227-1"><a href="#cite_note-auto1-227">[222]</a></sup> Canada,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-267"><a href="#cite_note-267">[262]</a></sup> and Asia.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Energy">Energy</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Energy_in_Ukraine" title="Energy in Ukraine">Energy in Ukraine</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:262px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Electricity-prod-source-stacked.svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="600" data-file-width="850" decoding="async" height="184" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fa/Electricity-prod-source-stacked.svg/260px-Electricity-prod-source-stacked.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fa/Electricity-prod-source-stacked.svg/390px-Electricity-prod-source-stacked.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fa/Electricity-prod-source-stacked.svg/520px-Electricity-prod-source-stacked.svg.png 2x" width="260"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Electricity-prod-source-stacked.svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Electricity production by source in Ukraine</div></div></div>
<p>Energy in Ukraine is mainly from <a href="/wiki/Natural_gas_in_Ukraine" title="Natural gas in Ukraine">gas</a> and <a href="/wiki/Coal_in_Ukraine" title="Coal in Ukraine">coal</a>, followed by <a href="/wiki/Nuclear_power_in_Ukraine" title="Nuclear power in Ukraine">nuclear</a> then oil.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:0_175-2"><a href="#cite_note-:0-175">[170]</a></sup> The coal industry has been disrupted by conflict.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-268"><a href="#cite_note-268">[263]</a></sup> Most gas and oil is imported, but since 2015 <a href="/wiki/Energy_policy" title="Energy policy">energy policy</a> has prioritised diversifying energy supply.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-269"><a href="#cite_note-269">[264]</a></sup>
</p><p>About half of <a href="/wiki/Electricity_generation" title="Electricity generation">electricity generation</a> is nuclear and a quarter coal.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:0_175-3"><a href="#cite_note-:0-175">[170]</a></sup> The largest <a href="/wiki/Nuclear_power_plant" title="Nuclear power plant">nuclear power plant</a> in Europe, the <a href="/wiki/Zaporizhzhia_Nuclear_Power_Plant" title="Zaporizhzhia Nuclear Power Plant">Zaporizhzhia Nuclear Power Plant</a>, is in Ukraine. <a href="/wiki/Fossil_fuel_subsidies" title="Fossil fuel subsidies">Fossil fuel subsidies</a> were US$2.2 billion in 2019.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-270"><a href="#cite_note-270">[265]</a></sup> Until the 2010s all of Ukraine's nuclear fuel came from Russia, but now most does not.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-271"><a href="#cite_note-271">[266]</a></sup>
</p><p>Although gas transit is declining, over 40 billion cubic metres (bcm) of <a href="/wiki/Natural_gas_in_Russia" title="Natural gas in Russia">Russian gas</a> flowed through Ukraine in 2021,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-272"><a href="#cite_note-272">[267]</a></sup> which was about a third of Russian exports to other European countries.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-273"><a href="#cite_note-273">[268]</a></sup> Some energy infrastructure was destroyed in the 2022 Russian invasion of Ukraine.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-274"><a href="#cite_note-274">[269]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-275"><a href="#cite_note-275">[270]</a></sup>
</p><p>In early 2022 Ukraine and <a href="/wiki/Energy_in_Moldova" title="Energy in Moldova">Moldova</a> decoupled their electricity grids from the <a href="/wiki/IPS/UPS#IPS" title="IPS/UPS">Integrated Power System</a> of Russia and <a href="/wiki/Energy_in_Belarus" title="Energy in Belarus">Belarus</a>; and the <a href="/wiki/European_Network_of_Transmission_System_Operators_for_Electricity" title="European Network of Transmission System Operators for Electricity">European Network of Transmission System Operators for Electricity</a> synchronized them with <a href="/wiki/Synchronous_grid_of_Continental_Europe" title="Synchronous grid of Continental Europe">continental Europe</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cbsnews-ukraine-grid_276-0"><a href="#cite_note-cbsnews-ukraine-grid-276">[271]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-277"><a href="#cite_note-277">[272]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Information_technology">Information technology</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_Ukraine#Information_technology" title="Economy of Ukraine">Economy of Ukraine § Information technology</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Internet_in_Ukraine" title="Internet in Ukraine">Internet in Ukraine</a></div>
<p>The internet in the country is robust because it is diverse.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:3_278-0"><a href="#cite_note-:3-278">[273]</a></sup> Key officials may use <a href="/wiki/Starlink" title="Starlink">Starlink</a> as backup.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:3_278-1"><a href="#cite_note-:3-278">[273]</a></sup> The IT industry contributed almost 5 per cent to Ukraine's GDP in 2021<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-279"><a href="#cite_note-279">[274]</a></sup> and in 2022 continued both inside and outside the country.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-280"><a href="#cite_note-280">[275]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Demographics">Demographics</span></h2>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Demographics_of_Ukraine" title="Demographics of Ukraine">Demographics of Ukraine</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ukrainians" title="Ukrainians">Ukrainians</a></div>
<div class="barbox tright" style="overflow-x: auto;">
