<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Notes">Notes</span></h2>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1054258005">.mw-parser-output .refbegin{font-size:90%;margin-bottom:0.5em}.mw-parser-output .refbegin-hanging-indents>ul{margin-left:0}.mw-parser-output .refbegin-hanging-indents>ul>li{margin-left:0;padding-left:3.2em;text-indent:-3.2em}.mw-parser-output .refbegin-hanging-indents ul,.mw-parser-output .refbegin-hanging-indents ul li{list-style:none}@media(max-width:720px){.mw-parser-output .refbegin-hanging-indents>ul>li{padding-left:1.6em;text-indent:-1.6em}}.mw-parser-output .refbegin-columns{margin-top:0.3em}.mw-parser-output .refbegin-columns ul{margin-top:0}.mw-parser-output .refbegin-columns li{page-break-inside:avoid;break-inside:avoid-column}</style><div class="refbegin refbegin-columns references-column-width" style="column-width: 30em">
<p><b>a.</b><style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1041539562">.mw-parser-output .citation{word-wrap:break-word}.mw-parser-output .citation:target{background-color:rgba(0,127,255,0.133)}</style><span class="citation wikicite" id="endnote_Anone"><a href="#ref_Anone"><b><sup>^</sup></b></a></span>  Among the Ukrainians that rose to the highest offices in the Russian Empire were <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Aleksey_Razumovsky" title="Aleksey Razumovsky">Aleksey Razumovsky</a>, <a href="/wiki/Alexander_Bezborodko" title="Alexander Bezborodko">Alexander Bezborodko</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ivan_Paskevich" title="Ivan Paskevich">Ivan Paskevich</a>. Among the Ukrainians who greatly influenced the <a href="/wiki/Russian_Orthodox_Church" title="Russian Orthodox Church">Russian Orthodox Church</a> in this period were <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Stephen_Yavorsky" title="Stephen Yavorsky">Stephen Yavorsky</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Feofan_Prokopovich" title="Feofan Prokopovich">Feofan Prokopovich</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dimitry_of_Rostov" title="Dimitry of Rostov">Dimitry of Rostov</a>.
</p><p><b>b.</b><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1041539562" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><span class="citation wikicite" id="endnote_Bnone"><a href="#ref_Bnone"><b><sup>^</sup></b></a></span>  Estimates on the number of deaths vary. Official Soviet data is not available because the Soviet government denied the existence of the famine. See the <a href="/wiki/Holodomor" title="Holodomor">Holodomor</a> article for details. Sources differ on interpreting various statements from different branches of different governments as to whether they amount to the official recognition of the Famine as Genocide by the country. For example, after the statement issued by the Latvian Sejm on 13 March 2008, the total number of countries is given as 19 (according to <i>Ukrainian <a href="/wiki/BBC" title="BBC">BBC</a></i>: <a class="external text" href="http://www.bbc.com/ukrainian/domestic/story/2008/03/080313_latvia_holodomor_oh.shtml" rel="nofollow"><span title="Ukrainian-language text"><span lang="uk">"Латвія визнала Голодомор ґеноцидом"</span></span></a>), 16 (according to <i><a href="/wiki/Korrespondent" title="Korrespondent">Korrespondent</a></i>, Russian edition: <a class="external text" href="http://korrespondent.net/ukraine/politics/403002" rel="nofollow"><span title="Russian-language text"><span lang="ru">"После продолжительных дебатов Сейм Латвии признал Голодомор геноцидом украинцев"</span></span></a>), "more than 10" (according to <i>Korrespondent</i>, Ukrainian edition: <a class="external text" href="http://ua.korrespondent.net/ukraine/403780-latviya-viznala-golodomor-1932-33-rr-genocidom-ukrayinciv" rel="nofollow"><span title="Ukrainian-language text"><span lang="uk">"Латвія визнала Голодомор 1932–33 рр. геноцидом українців"</span></span></a>) Retrieved 27 January 2008.
</p><p><b>c.</b><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1041539562" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><span class="citation wikicite" id="endnote_C1"><a href="#ref_C1"><b><sup>1</sup></b></a></span> <link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1041539562" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><span class="citation wikicite" id="endnote_C2"><a href="#ref_C2"><b><sup>2</sup></b></a></span>  These figures are likely to be much higher, as they <b>do not</b> include Ukrainians of other nationalities or Ukrainian Jews, but only <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ethnic" title="Ethnic">ethnic</a> Ukrainians, from the Ukrainian SSR.
</p><p><b>d.</b><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1041539562" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><span class="citation wikicite" id="endnote_Dnone"><a href="#ref_Dnone"><b><sup>^</sup></b></a></span>  This figure excludes <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/POW" title="POW">POW</a> deaths.
</p><p><b>e.</b><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1041539562" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><span class="citation wikicite" id="endnote_Enone"><a href="#ref_Enone"><b><sup>^</sup></b></a></span>  Several countries with territory in Europe have a larger total area, but all of those also include territory outside of Europe. Only Russia's European territory is larger than Ukraine.
</p><p><b>f.</b><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1041539562" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><span class="citation wikicite" id="endnote_F1"><a href="#ref_F1"><b><sup>1</sup></b></a></span> <link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1041539562" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><span class="citation wikicite" id="endnote_F2"><a href="#ref_F2"><b><sup>2</sup></b></a></span> <link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1041539562" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><span class="citation wikicite" id="endnote_F3"><a href="#ref_F3"><b><sup>3</sup></b></a></span>  According to the official <a href="/wiki/Ukrainian_Census_(2001)" title="Ukrainian Census (2001)">2001 census</a> data (by nationality;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-395"><a href="#cite_note-395">[390]</a></sup> by language<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-396"><a href="#cite_note-396">[391]</a></sup>) about 75 percent of Kyiv's population responded 'Ukrainian' to the native language (ridna mova) census question, and roughly 25 percent responded 'Russian'. On the other hand, when the question 'What language do you use in everyday life?' was asked in the 2003 sociological survey, the Kyivans' answers were distributed as follows: 'mostly Russian': 52 percent, 'both Russian and Ukrainian in equal measure': 32 percent, 'mostly Ukrainian': 14 percent, 'exclusively Ukrainian': 4.3 percent.<br/><style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1067248974">.mw-parser-output cite.citation{font-style:inherit;word-wrap:break-word}.mw-parser-output .citation q{quotes:"\"""\"""'""'"}.mw-parser-output </p><p><b>g.</b><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1041539562" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><span class="citation wikicite" id="endnote_Gnone"><a href="#ref_Gnone"><b><sup>^</sup></b></a></span>  Such writings were also the base for Russian and Belarusian literature.
</p>
</div>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1011085734">.mw-parser-output .reflist{font-size:90%;margin-bottom:0.5em;list-style-type:decimal}.mw-parser-output .reflist .references{font-size:100%;margin-bottom:0;list-style-type:inherit}.mw-parser-output .reflist-columns-2{column-width:30em}.mw-parser-output .reflist-columns-3{column-width:25em}.mw-parser-output .reflist-columns{margin-top:0.3em}.mw-parser-output .reflist-columns ol{margin-top:0}.mw-parser-output .reflist-columns li{page-break-inside:avoid;break-inside:avoid-column}.mw-parser-output .reflist-upper-alpha{list-style-type:upper-alpha}.mw-parser-output .reflist-upper-roman{list-style-type:upper-roman}.mw-parser-output .reflist-lower-alpha{list-style-type:lower-alpha}.mw-parser-output .reflist-lower-greek{list-style-type:lower-greek}.mw-parser-output .reflist-lower-roman{list-style-type:lower-roman}</style><div class="reflist">

</li>

The Defense of Ministry said the loss was "temporary".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16"><a href="#cite_note-16">[12]</a></sup> It has also lost control to the majority of its coastline around the Black Sea.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-17"><a href="#cite_note-17">[13]</a></sup></span>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="References">References</span></h2>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1011085734" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="reflist">
</div>

<li id="cite_note-131"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-131">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1067248974" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><cite class="citation web cs1"><a class="external text" href="https://2001-2009.state.gov/r/pa/ho/time/wwii/17604.htm" rel="nofollow">"United Nations"</a>. U.S. Department of State<span class="reference-accessdate">. Retrieved <span class="nowrap">22 September</span> 2014</span>. <q>Voting procedures and the veto power of permanent members of the Security Council were finalized at the <a href="/wiki/Yalta_Conference" title="Yalta Conference">Yalta Conference</a> in 1945 when Roosevelt and Stalin agreed that the veto would not prevent discussions by the Security Council. Roosevelt agreed to General Assembly membership for Ukraine and Byelorussia while reserving the right, which was never exercised, to seek two more votes for the United States.</q></cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=unknown&amp;rft.btitle=United+Nations&amp;rft.pub=U.S.+Department+of+State&amp;rft_id=https%3A%2F%2F2001-2009.state.gov%2Fr%2Fpa%2Fho%2Ftime%2Fwwii%2F17604.htm&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AUkraine"></span></span>

<li id="cite_note-132"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-132">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1067248974" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><cite class="citation web cs1"><a class="external text" href="https://2001-2009.state.gov/r/pa/ho/time/wwii/17604.htm" rel="nofollow">"United Nations"</a>. U.S. Department of State<span class="reference-accessdate">. Retrieved <span class="nowrap">22 September</span> 2014</span>. <q>Voting procedures and the veto power of permanent members of the Security Council were finalized at the Yalta Conference in 1945 when Roosevelt and Stalin agreed that the veto would not prevent discussions by the Security Council. In April 1945, new U.S. President Truman agreed to General Assembly membership for Ukraine and Byelorussia while reserving the right, which was never exercised, to seek two more votes for the United States.</q></cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=unknown&amp;rft.btitle=United+Nations&amp;rft.pub=U.S.+Department+of+State&amp;rft_id=https%3A%2F%2F2001-2009.state.gov%2Fr%2Fpa%2Fho%2Ftime%2Fwwii%2F17604.htm&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AUkraine"></span></span>
